7498217498122 URL = https://bugs.eclipse.org/bugs/show_bug.cgi?id=569619

The bug reproduces when validation is performed on one single EObject. The validation report has the same problem entries multiplied.

The problem comes from org.eclipse.sphinx.emf.validation.markers.ValidationMarkerManager.removeMarkers(EObject, int, String) method.

The markers are not removed because they are mistakenly not considered in org.eclipse.sphinx.emf.validation.markers.ValidationMarkerManager.getValidationMarkersList(EObject, int, String)  due to the fragmented URI of the object ( the check at line 501) returned by org.eclipse.sphinx.emf.validation.util.ValidationUtil.getURI(EObject).

The proposed solution would be to use the extended URI in org.eclipse.sphinx.emf.validation.util.ValidationUtil.getURI(EObject), by calling org.eclipse.sphinx.emf.util.EcoreResourceUtil.getURI(EObject, true) instead of org.eclipse.sphinx.emf.util.EcoreResourceUtil.getURI(EObject).

Note: the used Sphinx version is 0.11.2.

Hi, 

Tehre are several messages on the forum which indicates how to make the Linux and macOS versions of the Capella bundles works :

* Installation issue Mac OSX: 
    * https://forum.mbse-capella.org/t/installation-issue-mac-osx/3873/
* Installation procedure for Capella 1.1.0 on Mac OS
    * https://forum.mbse-capella.org/t/installation-procedure-for-capella-1-1-0-on-mac-os/3333
* Detailed instructions to run Capella 1.2.x on MacOS
    * https://forum.mbse-capella.org/t/detailed-instructions-to-run-capella-1-2-x-on-macos/3577
* Install capella in ubuntu 18.04
    * https://forum.mbse-capella.org/t/install-capella-in-ubuntu-18-04/3592/


The main step it to do a chmod O+x on the the eclipse executable. 

For 5.0, this additional step will have to be modified as the packaging has changed: 
* the executable is now named capella and is in the capella folder (the eclipse subfolder no more exists).
* the JRE is directly packaged in the bundle, the Java executables will need the same modification. 

A first lead is to modify the build to produce a tar.gz archive instead of a zip to keep the autorizations on the files/scripts (see for example Eclipse Rust 2020-09)


The Capella studio might need the same changes.

7498217498122 URL = https://bugs.eclipse.org/bugs/show_bug.cgi?id=569351



7498217498122 URL = https://bugs.eclipse.org/bugs/show_bug.cgi?id=569436

The class org.eclipse.papyrus.cdo.internal.ui.customization.properties.storage.CDOTextURIHandler allows to open input or output streams from URIs pointing to CDO Character Large Objects (CLobs). 
In practice it allows to easily open/modify/save EMF XMI Resources stored as CDOTextResource.

This class has been defined for an intial purpose related to Papyrus Properties View configuration, but it can  indeed be useful in other context. 
We propose to move it to org.eclipse.papyrus.cdo.core

In addition to that, we also provide ClobEditorInputToURIAdapterFactory whose goal is to adapt a CDOLobEditorInput into an EMF URI. 
This mechanism allows EMF editors (relying on org.eclipse.emf.edit.ui.util.EditUIUtil.getURI(IEditorInput) ) to get the URI of the EMF model from the CDOLobEditorInput  provided by the CDO Explorer.

Hence, the registration of CDOTextURIHandler in the resourceSet of the editingdomain of an EMF editor combined with the registration of the ClobEditorInputToURIAdapterFactory in the plaform adapter framework allows to open quite easily EMF models stored as text resources in EMF.

7498217498122 URL = https://bugs.eclipse.org/bugs/show_bug.cgi?id=569623

Rationale: 
Currently in DARC, the user can create Threats of 5 types that follow Chorus guidelines (Eavesdropping, Tampering, ...). However, these are not necessarily the types used by the projects due to constraints imposed by the customer and/or country regulations. At least 3 new types of Threats have been identified: Cloning, Retro-engineering, Accountability. This list may evolve as the tool is used by other users.

An alternative to the full customization of Threat types could be an attribute on the Threat which values could be defined by the user. This attribute would be a Threat "sub-type".


* Metamodel (M2) changes
        - to allow user be able to edit / add / remove its threat kind values
* Property views (display a radiobox for each values defined in enumeration)
* model migration
* Check when user add a new enumeration literal, property view is properly updated
* Layers Security Needs to change color according to index of value

7498217498122 URL = https://bugs.eclipse.org/bugs/show_bug.cgi?id=569411

An external report identified a vulnerability in the Eclipse Paho MQTT for C configuration for connecting devices) not checking server hostname when connecting using tlsio_openssl. Exploiting this vulnerability requires the attacker to be positioned between the client and server and cannot be exploited remotely.

MQTTClient_SSLOptions_initializer should have the verify option enabled by default (we’ve tested that enableServerCertAuth is enabled by default but will not perform hostname validation).

Example:

MQTTClient_SSLOptions mqtt_ssl_options = MQTTClient_SSLOptions_initializer;
mqtt_ssl_options.verify = 1; // Adds hostname validation.
mqtt_ssl_options.enableServerCertAuth = 1; // Enabled by default. Won’t authenticate the server: it only validates the CA chain validity – name is misleading.

Code location: eclipse/paho.mqtt.c: An Eclipse Paho C client library for MQTT for Windows, Linux and MacOS. (github.com):

  /**
     * Whether to carry out post-connect checks, including that a certificate
     * matches the given host name.
     * Exists only if struct_version >= 2
     */
    int verify;

#define MQTTClient_SSLOptions_initializer { {'M', 'Q', 'T', 'S'}, 5, NULL, NULL, NULL, NULL, NULL, 1, MQTT_SSL_VERSION_DEFAULT, 0, NULL, NULL, NULL, NULL, NULL, 0, NULL, 0 }

Microsoft is shipping a related fix across all products in our upcoming December Security Update on 2020-DEC-08.

Microsoft 1st party code takes dependency on Paho MQTT. We need to ingest your fix in order to complete shipping the fix in all areas to ensure customers can get secure. Please advise when update will push to repositories. Please reference MSRC Case # 62416 in all correspondence with secure@microsoft.com

P. Switzer
MSRC Sr Security PM

7498217498122 URL = https://bugs.eclipse.org/bugs/show_bug.cgi?id=569057

Rationale: Currently DARC visualizes functional and logical trust boundaries. But not Physical ones. Also, the fire icon representing the trust boundaries is not visible enough.

- Change decoration style from a ! red bold label and a more highlighted icon

- Add same decoration on PhysicalLinks (PL) :  decorator Cybersecurity Trust Boundaries Layer

ComponentExchange (CE) are colored if :
source or target component is not trusted
OR if one of its allocatedFunctionalExchanges is not trusted 
PhysicalLinks (PL) are colored if :
source or target component is not trusted
OR if one of its allocatedComponentExchanges is not trusted
- Junits

7498217498122 URL = https://bugs.eclipse.org/bugs/show_bug.cgi?id=569283

Steps to reproduce:
1. Create an activity with an activity diagram containing some actions (for example opaque actions).
2. Add some control flow edges between the actions.
3. Select all actions (or a subset of them), but not the surrounding activity itself, and apply "Arrange Selection" from the toolbar or from the context menu.
4. The actions will then be rearranged so that some of them are moved outside the containing activity node and be invisible in the diagram.
Repeating the "Arrange selection" command makes it even worse.

The expected behavior would be that the actions are rearranged within the surrounding activity compartment.

7498217498122 URL = https://bugs.eclipse.org/bugs/show_bug.cgi?id=569581

Created attachment 285003 [details]
Example CDT project to reproduce the problem with, see description for reproduction steps.

During one of our CDT-related tests we observed sporadic IOExceptions logged in ElfParser.hasInterpProgramHeader(), without any actual loss of functionality.

Upon investigation those seem to be caused by a consecutive build called in the test, colliding with CModelManager work started by a previous build called from the test. In particular the 2nd build would delete .so files that were being visited due to the first build.

To reproduce:

1. Have a Makefile project that use an .so file, e.g. import the one from the attached archive "".
2. Set a breakpoint at the call to super() in the constructor of ERandomAccessFile: org.eclipse.cdt.utils.ERandomAccessFile.ERandomAccessFile(String, String)
3. Trigger a build on the Makefile project.
4. Observe breakpoint hit.
5. Delete the .so file that is being parsed.
6. Resume breakpoint.
7. Observe logged exception:
!ENTRY org.eclipse.cdt.core 4 0 2020-12-09 14:22:03.320
!MESSAGE Error: /data/tmp/cdt_runtime_ws/TestMakefile/libencoder.so (No such file or directory)
!STACK 0
java.io.FileNotFoundException: /data/tmp/cdt_runtime_ws/TestMakefile/libencoder.so (No such file or directory)
	at java.base/java.io.RandomAccessFile.open0(Native Method)
	at java.base/java.io.RandomAccessFile.open(RandomAccessFile.java:345)
	at java.base/java.io.RandomAccessFile.<init>(RandomAccessFile.java:259)
	at java.base/java.io.RandomAccessFile.<init>(RandomAccessFile.java:214)
	at java.base/java.io.RandomAccessFile.<init>(RandomAccessFile.java:127)
	at org.eclipse.cdt.utils.ERandomAccessFile.<init>(ERandomAccessFile.java:32)
	at org.eclipse.cdt.utils.elf.Elf.commonSetup(Elf.java:690)
	at org.eclipse.cdt.utils.elf.Elf.<init>(Elf.java:711)
	at org.eclipse.cdt.utils.elf.parser.ElfParser.getPHdrs(ElfParser.java:187)
	at org.eclipse.cdt.utils.elf.parser.ElfParser.hasInterpProgramHeader(ElfParser.java:179)
	at org.eclipse.cdt.utils.elf.parser.ElfParser.getBinary(ElfParser.java:63)
	at org.eclipse.cdt.internal.core.model.CModelManager.createBinaryFile(CModelManager.java:785)
	at org.eclipse.cdt.internal.core.model.BinaryRunner$Visitor.visit(BinaryRunner.java:226)
	at org.eclipse.core.internal.resources.Resource.lambda$0(Resource.java:85)
	at org.eclipse.core.internal.watson.ElementTreeIterator.doIteration(ElementTreeIterator.java:85)
	at org.eclipse.core.internal.watson.ElementTreeIterator.doIteration(ElementTreeIterator.java:90)
	at org.eclipse.core.internal.watson.ElementTreeIterator.iterate(ElementTreeIterator.java:135)
	at org.eclipse.core.internal.resources.Resource.accept(Resource.java:94)
	at org.eclipse.core.internal.resources.Resource.accept(Resource.java:55)
	at org.eclipse.cdt.internal.core.model.BinaryRunner$1.run(BinaryRunner.java:121)
	at org.eclipse.core.internal.jobs.Worker.run(Worker.java:63)

The code that logs the exception was added here:

https://bugs.eclipse.org/bugs/show_bug.cgi?id=512822

See: org.eclipse.cdt.utils.elf.parser.ElfParser.hasInterpProgramHeader(byte[], IPath)

try {
	/* No PHdr.PT_INTERP found in the hints meaning we need to read the file itself */
	return Arrays.stream(getPHdrs(path)).anyMatch(phdr -> phdr.p_type == PHdr.PT_INTERP);
} catch (IOException e) {
	CCorePlugin.log(e);
}

Instead of logging and worse, hiding, the IOException, the method should leave exception handling to the caller: ElfParser.getBinary(). There the exception is re-thrown under some conditions:

} catch (IOException e) {
	if (hints == null) {
		try {
			binary = createBinaryArchive(path);
		} catch (IOException e2) {
			CCorePlugin.log(e); // log original exception
			throw e2;
		}
	}
}

Note that the line above commented with "log original exception" might result in undesired logging; that should be handled in a separate bug.

7498217498122 URL = https://bugs.eclipse.org/bugs/show_bug.cgi?id=569076

7498217498122 URL = https://bugs.eclipse.org/bugs/show_bug.cgi?id=568963

Hey,

A while back, I asked quite a few questions regarding performance and VIATRA [1]. I made the observation that there existed two specific elements of which the removal took quite a lot of time. 

I figured out the performance bottleneck! 

Apparently, delayUpdatePropagation() can cause quite some overhead in some cases. Although I yet have to rerun my performance benchmarks again, on my work computer the removal of a central model entity went down from ~85s to ~12s. 

Perhaps this is to be expected due to some underwater computations being done. However, in this case I think it would be good to mention this in the documentation.

- Hans

[1] https://www.eclipse.org/forums/index.php/t/1105611/

7498217498122 URL = https://bugs.eclipse.org/bugs/show_bug.cgi?id=569238

"xsd2ttcn -h" creates cyclical type definitions when one of the choices in a complexType choice is restricted to the type of another choice.

Consider the following .xsd file:

<?xml version="1.0" encoding="utf-8"?>
<xs:schema xmlns:xs="http://www.w3.org/2001/XMLSchema"
xmlns="http://uri/test2"
targetNamespace="http://uri/test2"
version="2.4.1"
elementFormDefault="qualified"
>
    <xs:simpleType name="IMSI">
        <xs:restriction base="xs:token">
            <xs:pattern value="[0-9]{6,15}"/>
        </xs:restriction>
    </xs:simpleType>
    <xs:simpleType name="SUPIIMSI">
        <xs:restriction base="IMSI"/>
    </xs:simpleType>
</xs:schema>

Using xsd2ttcn -h on this creates one type for IMSI (a restricted XSD.token charstring) and one type for SUPIIMSI (type alias of IMSI):

type XSD.Token IMSI (pattern "[0-9]#(6,15)");
type IMSI SUPIIMSI;

Now consider the same file, with an additional type:

<?xml version="1.0" encoding="utf-8"?>
<xs:schema xmlns:xs="http://www.w3.org/2001/XMLSchema"
xmlns="http://uri/test"
targetNamespace="http://uri/test"
version="2.4.1"
elementFormDefault="qualified"
>
    <xs:simpleType name="IMSI">
        <xs:restriction base="xs:token">
            <xs:pattern value="[0-9]{6,15}"/>
        </xs:restriction>
    </xs:simpleType>
    <xs:simpleType name="SUPIIMSI">
        <xs:restriction base="IMSI"/>
    </xs:simpleType>
    <xs:complexType name="TargetIdentifier">
        <xs:choice>
		<xs:element name="imsi" type="IMSI"/>
		<xs:element name="supiimsi" type="SUPIIMSI"/>
        </xs:choice>
    </xs:complexType>
</xs:schema>

Using xsd2ttcn -h on this will create a cyclical type definition (IMSI_derivations contains itself, as SUPIIMSI is IMSI_derivations):

type XSD.Token IMSI (pattern "[0-9]#(6,15)");
type IMSI_derivations SUPIIMSI;
type union IMSI_derivations
{
  IMSI iMSI,
  SUPIIMSI sUPIIMSI
}
with {
  variant "useType";
  variant (iMSI) "name as capitalized";
  variant (sUPIIMSI) "name as capitalized";
};

Normally, the "derivations" created by the -h flag are needed to make sure that various types extending another type can be used everywhere where that type is used, but here, since SUPIIMSI is restricted by the type IMSI, it seems like no IMSI_derivations should have been created in this case. The derivation becomes cyclical.

(I should add that we are trying to generate ETSI X1 protocol files from official ETSI specifications. The X1 xsd file requires the flag -h in order to create useful definitions, but it also uses the ETSI Types xsd, which contains the SUPIIMSI definition.)

7498217498122 URL = https://bugs.eclipse.org/bugs/show_bug.cgi?id=568902

As reported in this forum post: https://www.eclipse.org/forums/index.php/t/1105240/

The timerhandler will calculate the next activation time only after acquiring a mutex. This can lead to a delayed calculation of the activation time and to jitter. Therefore this should be done before the mutex.

Furthermore the timerhandler is acquiring in each activation a mutex. By replacing this with a separate queue the mutex would only be needed if new elements are added and this would greatly reduce the computation power and delay introduced by the timer handler. With that we expect a further reduction of the jitter of the timerhandler.

7498217498122 URL = https://bugs.eclipse.org/bugs/show_bug.cgi?id=569693

The filtering add-on hooks several parts of Capella and/or Sirius to brings its capabilities. 

Some mecanisms are installed and reacts to changes even if the Filtering Viewpoint is not enabled on the current Capella project. The impact on performance is lower on "non Capella" Sirius projects as it seems that the presence of Capella elements is checked.

For example, on a project with 111 000 elements in the Capella model and 440 diagrams, in a Capella 1.4.0 with Filtering add-on installed but not enabled (Sirius Viewpoint) nor referenced (KitlAlpha Viewpoint Manager), changing the background color of a component on a LAB diagram with 486 DDiagramElements takes twice the time to do the same change when the Filtering add-on is not installed.

The impact seems to be visible on several user interaction : routing style change, color changes, element addition on a diagram, move/resize/layout changes, paste format, ...

The performance degradation are increased with the size of the model, the size of the diagram and the number of selected elements.

7498217498122 URL = https://bugs.eclipse.org/bugs/show_bug.cgi?id=569306

Ref : https://openjdk.java.net/jeps/390 


Short Description from the feature info:

The primitive wrapper classes in java.lang (Byte, Short, Integer, Long, Float, Double, Boolean, and Character) have been designated as value-based.

To discourage misuse of value-based class instances:

The primitive wrapper class constructors, originally deprecated in Java 9, have been deprecated for removal. Wherever the constructors are called in source, javac by default produces removal warnings. The jdeprscan tool may be used to identify usage of deprecated APIs in binaries.

javac implements a new warning category, synchronization, which identifies usages of the synchronized statement with an operand of a value-based class type, or of a type whose subtypes are all specified to be value-based. The warning category is turned on by default, and can be manually selected with -Xlint:synchronization.

7498217498122 URL = https://bugs.eclipse.org/bugs/show_bug.cgi?id=569582

Rationale: Currently in DARC, the user can create Threats of 5 types that follow Chorus guidelines (Eavesdropping, Tampering, ...). However, these are not necessarily the types used by the projects due to constraints imposed by the customer and/or country regulations. At least 3 new types of Threats have been identified: Cloning, Retro-engineering, Accountability. This list may evolve as the tool is used by other users.

An alternative to the full customisation of Threat types could be an attribute on the Threat which values could be defined by the user. This attribute would be a Threat "sub-type".

  * Add in the Cybersecurity Configuration packaga, a property for threat kind (enumeration type), and the user can customize the types by adding literals to this type.

7498217498122 URL = https://bugs.eclipse.org/bugs/show_bug.cgi?id=569624

Titan Designer plug-in (version "7/CAX 105 7730 R2A (7.2.pl0)", but this page would not allow me to select higher than 7.1.0) shows an invalid error marker:

  “Refence to a value or template was expected instead of port”

when a port array is used in log2str. Titan transforms this without problem to a string so that port name can be used in the log, so this code is valid.

Minimal example:

import from IPL4asp_PortType all;

type component Minimal_CT
{
    port IPL4asp_PT array_PT[1]
    port IPL4asp_PT single_PT
}

testcase tc_log_port()
runs on Minimal_CT
{
    setverdict(pass);

    // No error markers:
    log(single_PT);
    log(log2str("Port named :", single_PT));
    var charstring vl_logstring_1 := log2str("Port named :", single_PT);

    // Error markers on all:
    log(array_PT[0]);
    log(log2str("Port named :", array_PT[0]));
    var charstring vl_logstring_2 := log2str("Port named :", array_PT[0]);
}

A new annotation wrapping settings have been added in 4.18 (Line Wrapping > Wrapping Settings > Annotations), but it looks like these settings are reset every time user edits current formatter settings.

How to reproduce:
1. have Eclipse platform with JDT installed
2. run Eclipse
3. make sure formatter settings (Preferences > Java > Code Style > Formatter > Edit...) for e.g. type is set as follows:
  * Line Wrapping > Wrapping Settings > Annotations: On types is set to 'Do not wrap'
4. click on 'Apply' then 'OK' and then 'Apply and Close'
5. open the formatter settings again (Preferences > Java > Code Style > Formatter > Edit...)

Now the formatting of 'Line Wrapping > Wrapping Settings > Annotations: On types' is back to it's default value 'Wrap all elements, every element on a new line'.

My configuration:
Eclipse Platform 4.18 (I20201202-1800)
Eclipse Java Development Tools 3.18.600.v20201125-1800	
Java version: 11.0.9.1

line number may not perfectly align with JDT's master.

This appears to be between these fixes:

Bug 526310 introduced an unsafe cast from Consumer<IModuleUpdate> to AddReads, see https://git.eclipse.org/c/jdt/eclipse.jdt.core.git/diff/org.eclipse.jdt.core/model/org/eclipse/jdt/internal/core/builder/State.java?id=eb21f442c8cee0fdeff4a227bd4bb4fef58f9a52

Bug 224708 inserts a lambda into the map of module updates, likely it's this lambda that failed the cast, although another lambda exists in the same class. See https://git.eclipse.org/c/jdt/eclipse.jdt.core.git/diff/org.eclipse.jdt.core/model/org/eclipse/jdt/internal/core/ModuleUpdater.java?id=56091bab8ca0004cc67f7a12186fd7908110d6e9

Most recently, bug 567532 ensured that module-updates are persisted in the state also for test folders. This exposes the lambda from bug 224708 to the unsafe cast from 526310.

7498217498122 URL = https://bugs.eclipse.org/bugs/show_bug.cgi?id=569731

Given this code

    switch (targetType) {
    case 100: // comment 0
        x = 0;
        break;
    case 101: // comment 1  
        x = 1;
        break;
    }

apply quick fix "Convert 'switch' to 'if-else'". Comments are lost:

    if (targetType == 100) {
        x = 0;
    } else if (targetType == 101) {
        x = 1;
    }

7498217498122 URL = https://bugs.eclipse.org/bugs/show_bug.cgi?id=568942

In Preferences > Java > Code Style > Formatter, one can edit the profile.  In the Indentation > align items in columns, please add the ability to align parameters.  For example, please change this code...

map.put("apple", "red");
map.put("banana", "yellow");
map.put("grape", "green");
map.put("orange", "orange");
map.put("pear", "green");

... into this code ...

map.put("apple",  "red");
map.put("banana", "yellow");
map.put("grape",  "green");
map.put("orange", "orange");
map.put("pear",   "green");

This is a simple example.  When there are many more parameters in a method, then aligning the parameters in columns helps a lot with readability.

Eclipse launcher is currently built with macOS 10.12 SDK. We should build it with macOS 10.14 SDK. 
It think it'll help in better theming support. Also, the behaviour of base SDK and child SDK will be closer.

We’ll use this Bugzilla record to track the onboarding process for the project. This channel will be the primary means of communication for the project team, your mentors, and the Eclipse Foundation during this process. 
 
To get started on your new project, we need to do the following:
-Ensure that all of the committers listed on the proposal have Eclipse Foundation Accounts [1]
-Identify a mentor for the project

We will open separate Bugzilla records to track this.
 
Once we have all of the requirements above and the proposal has been open for community review for a minimum of two weeks, we will schedule the project for creation. If you have any questions for us, please feel free to reach out anytime! As well, if you’d like an overview of the project creation process, check out our Project Handbook [2].

We look forward to working with you and your team to make this project a success! 
 
[1] https://accounts.eclipse.org/user/register
[2] https://www.eclipse.org/projects/handbook/#starting

7498217498122 URL = https://bugs.eclipse.org/bugs/show_bug.cgi?id=569562

jdt uses a number of times simple synchronized access instead of the faster double-check ideom for instance fields.

If you need high-performance lazy initializing of an instance field, use
the double-check idiom with a volatile field. This idiom wasn't
guaranteed to work until release 5.0, when the platform got a new memory
model. The idiom is very fast but also complicated and delicate, so
don't be tempted to modify it in any way. Just copy and paste --
normally not a good idea, but appropriate here:

// Double-check idiom for lazy initialization of instance fields.
private volatile FieldType field;
FieldType getField() {
    FieldType result = field;
    if (result == null) { // First check (no locking)
        synchronized(this) {
            result = field;
            if (result == null) // Second check (with locking)
                field = result = computeFieldValue();
        }
    }
     return result;
}

see https://www.oracle.com/technical-resources/articles/javase/bloch-effective-08-qa.html

public class Test {

		}

		private Inner(Supplier<Object> o) {}
	}
}
```

```

7498217498122 URL = https://bugs.eclipse.org/bugs/show_bug.cgi?id=569522

Hi all,
this code doesn't currently compile

public class SealedVsGenericBug {
  sealed interface Foo<T> permits Bar { }
  final class Bar<T> implements Foo<T> { }
}

Eclipse currently asks that Bar that follows "permtis" to be a parametrized type,
here are the reported errors:
- Permitted type Bar does not declare SealedVsGenericBug.Foo<T> as direct super interface
- The type Bar extending a sealed class SealedVsGenericBug.Foo<T> should be a permitted subtype of SealedVsGenericBug.Foo<T>

It doesn't work that way, permitted subtypes are names not types.

This code also compiles fine with javac.

7498217498122 URL = https://bugs.eclipse.org/bugs/show_bug.cgi?id=569698

I just started with a fresh installation of Eclipse for Java Developers. It contains both M2E and EGit, which is just what I need.

I think this connector should be part of each Eclipse build containing both M2E and EGit.

7498217498122 URL = https://bugs.eclipse.org/bugs/show_bug.cgi?id=569434

First of all I'm uncertain this is a bug in Equinox and it could do anything against it, still I thought I write a ticket so at least it is documented somewhere.

While porting an application to Java-11 we came across a problem with CompletableFuture and Buddy-Classloading which we use to get Remote EJBs running.

The problem is that JBoss-Client-jar using the ThreadContextClassLoader to look up classes. This probably just worked by luck in Java-8 but is broken starting with Java-9 (see https://bugs.java.com/bugdatabase/view_bug.do?bug_id=JDK-8172726). 

In Java-8 the ThreadContextClassLoader was set to org.eclipse.osgi.internal.framework.ContextFinder and in Java-11 it is a the SystemClassLoader, so code like the JBoss-Client-jar who relied on the ThreadContextClassLoader is now broken.

I'll probably file a ticket againt jboss-marshaling as well but as I guess there's more code in the world using ThreadContextClassLoader if there's a chance to get this fixed in Equinox that would be great.

One can test that yourself fairly easily running the following simple app:

---------------8<---------------
public class Application implements IApplication {

	@Override
	public Object start(IApplicationContext context) throws Exception {
		System.err.println("parent thread --- " + Thread.currentThread().getContextClassLoader());
		
		CompletableFuture.runAsync(() -> System.err
				.println("CompletableFuture.runAync --- " + Thread.currentThread().getContextClassLoader()));
		
		new Thread(
				() -> System.err.println("new Thread().start() --- " + Thread.currentThread().getContextClassLoader()))
						.start();
		
		Timer t = new Timer();
		t.schedule(new TimerTask() {
			
			@Override
			public void run() {
				System.err.println("TimerTask: "  + Thread.currentThread().getContextClassLoader());
			}
		}, 1000);

		final Job job = new Job("testJob") { //$NON-NLS-1$
			@Override
			protected IStatus run(IProgressMonitor monitor) {
				System.err.println("new Job().schedule() --- " + Thread.currentThread().getContextClassLoader());
				return Status.OK_STATUS;
			};
		};

		job.schedule();
		System.in.read();
		return IApplication.EXIT_OK;
	}

	@Override
	public void stop() {
		// nothing to do
	}
}
---------------8<---------------

On Java-8 that prints:
---------------8<---------------
parent thread --- org.eclipse.osgi.internal.framework.ContextFinder@437da279
CompletableFuture.runAync --- org.eclipse.osgi.internal.framework.ContextFinder@437da279
new Thread().start() --- org.eclipse.osgi.internal.framework.ContextFinder@437da279
new Job().schedule() --- org.eclipse.osgi.internal.framework.ContextFinder@437da279
TimerTask: org.eclipse.osgi.internal.framework.ContextFinder@437da279
---------------8<---------------

On Java-11 that prints:
---------------8<---------------
parent thread --- org.eclipse.osgi.internal.framework.ContextFinder@f56244eb
CompletableFuture.runAync --- jdk.internal.loader.ClassLoaders$AppClassLoader@3f92f899
new Thread().start() --- org.eclipse.osgi.internal.framework.ContextFinder@f56244eb
new Job().schedule() --- org.eclipse.osgi.internal.framework.ContextFinder@f56244eb
TimerTask: org.eclipse.osgi.internal.framework.ContextFinder@f56244eb
---------------8<---------------

A current workaround we are looking into is to replace the "ForkJoinWorkerThreadFactory" at runtime but that does not feel go either

7498217498122 URL = https://bugs.eclipse.org/bugs/show_bug.cgi?id=569336

The original user scenario is from https://github.com/eclipse/eclipse.jdt.ls/issues/1157.

Currently JDT only supports custom options at the project and workspace level, which is fine for Eclipse use. However, as more and more clients use JDT through the JDT Language Server, it is necessary to allow custom options at the file level.

For example, some clients support specifying indentation, such as using spaces or tabs as indentation for each Java file, which may be different from the parent project. But when the language server suggests a code action for such a Java file, it still uses the project's options to generate the text edit instead of using the file's indentation. The user will see the inconsistent formatting. This is because code actions read formatting options from the compiled unit's project by default. See the rewriteAST() method in the file ASTRewrite.java.

public TextEdit rewriteAST() throws JavaModelException, IllegalArgumentException {
    ASTNode rootNode= getRootNode();
    if (rootNode == null) {
        return new MultiTextEdit(); // no changes
    }

    ASTNode root= rootNode.getRoot();
    if (!(root instanceof CompilationUnit)) {
        throw new IllegalArgumentException("This API can only be used if the AST is created from a compilation unit or class file"); //$NON-NLS-1$
    }
    CompilationUnit astRoot= (CompilationUnit) root;
    ITypeRoot typeRoot = astRoot.getTypeRoot();
    if (typeRoot == null || typeRoot.getBuffer() == null) {
        throw new IllegalArgumentException("This API can only be used if the AST is created from a compilation unit or class file"); //$NON-NLS-1$
    }

    char[] content= typeRoot.getBuffer().getCharacters();
    LineInformation lineInfo= LineInformation.create(astRoot);
    String lineDelim= typeRoot.findRecommendedLineSeparator();
    Map options= typeRoot.getJavaProject().getOptions(true);   // <=== Fetch the options from the project by default.

    return internalRewriteAST(content, lineInfo, lineDelim, astRoot.getCommentList(), options, rootNode, (RecoveryScannerData)astRoot.getStatementsRecoveryData());
}

One proposal is to allow specifying custom options at ICompilationUnit, such as adding two methods getOptions() and setOptions() to the ICompilationUnit interface, which can be used to save the custom formatting options for each Java file. This is similar as custom options at IJavaProject level.

/**
 * Sets the ICompilationUnit custom options. All and only the options explicitly included in the given table
 * are remembered; all previous option settings are forgotten, including ones not explicitly
 * mentioned.
 * <p>
 * For a complete description of the configurable options, see <code>JavaCore#getDefaultOptions</code>.
 * </p>
 *
 * @param newOptions the new options (key type: <code>String</code>; value type: <code>String</code>),
 *   or <code>null</code> to flush all custom options (clients will automatically get the global JavaCore options).
 * @see JavaCore#getDefaultOptions()
 */
void setOptions(Map<String, String> newOptions);

/**
 * Returns the table of the current custom options for this ICompilationUnit. ICompilationUnit remember their custom options,
 * in other words, only the options different from the JavaProject and JavaCore global options for the workspace.
 * A boolean argument allows to directly merge the ICompilationUnit options with the project and global ones from <code>JavaCore</code>.
 * <p>
 * For a complete description of the configurable options, see <code>JavaCore#getDefaultOptions</code>.
 * </p>
 *
 * @param inheritJavaCoreOptions - boolean indicating whether project and JavaCore options should be inherited as well
 * @return table of current settings of all options
 *   (key type: <code>String</code>; value type: <code>String</code>)
 * @see JavaCore#getDefaultOptions()
 */
Map<String, String> getOptions(boolean inheritJavaCoreOptions);


Then when the ASTRewriter creates the text edit, it could read the formatting from the ICompilationUnit.

public TextEdit rewriteAST() throws JavaModelException, IllegalArgumentException {
    ASTNode rootNode= getRootNode();
    if (rootNode == null) {
        return new MultiTextEdit(); // no changes
    }

    ASTNode root= rootNode.getRoot();
    if (!(root instanceof CompilationUnit)) {
        throw new IllegalArgumentException("This API can only be used if the AST is created from a compilation unit or class file"); //$NON-NLS-1$
    }
    CompilationUnit astRoot= (CompilationUnit) root;
    ITypeRoot typeRoot = astRoot.getTypeRoot();
    if (typeRoot == null || typeRoot.getBuffer() == null) {
        throw new IllegalArgumentException("This API can only be used if the AST is created from a compilation unit or class file"); //$NON-NLS-1$
    }

    char[] content= typeRoot.getBuffer().getCharacters();
    LineInformation lineInfo= LineInformation.create(astRoot);
    String lineDelim= typeRoot.findRecommendedLineSeparator();

    // =====> Add new code here
    Map options = typeRoot instanceof ICompilationUnit) ? ((ICompilationUnit) typeRoot).getOptions(true) :
            typeRoot.getJavaProject().getOptions(true);

    return internalRewriteAST(content, lineInfo, lineDelim, astRoot.getCommentList(), options, rootNode, (RecoveryScannerData)astRoot.getStatementsRecoveryData());
}

7498217498122 URL = https://bugs.eclipse.org/bugs/show_bug.cgi?id=568864

Linux HiDPI GC.fillGradientRectangle sets device scale permanently

Linux Ubuntu 20.04
Hi-res display (200% scaling)

I am creating an SWT Image to a GC instance usng fillGradientRectangle() and drawing text to the same GC instance.

However, any GC methods used after calling fillGradientRectangle() draw at double-scale.

- Run the attached snippet and look at the generated image
- drawText() is called first and draws correctly
- fillGradientRectangle() is then called
- drawText() is then called again, but this time scaling is at 2x and so the text is double size
- If fillGradientRectangle() is commented out, then drawing is at the correct scale

It seems that once GC#fillGradientRectangle() is called any drawing after that is at double scale.

Note these lines in GC#fillGradientRectangleInPixels() :

if (DPIUtil.useCairoAutoScale() ) {
...
Cairo.cairo_surface_set_device_scale(surface, scaleFactor, scaleFactor);

Perhaps the scale should be set back to its original setting after drawing the gradient?

7498217498122 URL = https://bugs.eclipse.org/bugs/show_bug.cgi?id=568966

In Eclipse you can define overlapping source folders for a Java project via the "Java Build Path" dialog like this:
* Folder "src"; included all; excluded none (default source folder)
* Folder "."; included "model/", exluded "src/" (added manually)

In the .classpath file you then get:
<classpathentry kind="src" path="src"/>
<classpathentry kind="src" path="" excluding="src/" including="model/"/>

In the Maven pom.xml I would define it like this:
<build>
	<sourceDirectory>src</sourceDirectory>
	<resources>
		<resource>
			<directory>model</directory>
		</resource>
	</resources>
</build>

When configuring the project, m2e logs "Skipping resource folder [...]" and does not add the resource directory to the classpath.

The reason is https://github.com/eclipse-m2e/m2e-core/blob/d53d22d98f2ac6d1f7124e146df8ed6fb22f6a75/org.eclipse.m2e.jdt/src/org/eclipse/m2e/jdt/internal/AbstractJavaProjectConfigurator.java#L467 (verified by debugging). The source code comment hints this was implemented to prevent a Java Model Exception.

To my mind it is possible to check the validity with more detail so that the configuration from the POM as stated above would work.

If you agree on this I could try to come up with a pull request.

7498217498122 URL = https://bugs.eclipse.org/bugs/show_bug.cgi?id=569660

If I press CTRL-SPACE to open content assist in the page designer it last over a second until the content assist popup is shown. The more properties or methods a JSF managed bean has the wrose the time gets.

The problem is that for each proposal in the content assist list the additional proposal info is computed before the list is displayed. 

In most cases the additional proposal info contains the javadoc of the underlying method or bean. If on a method no  javadoc is defined then a type hierarchy is build to get the javadoc of the overloaded method. This takes a lot of time (a few milliseconds each) 

Note, that on the content assist popup only the additional info of the currently selected entry is displayed. Therefore computing the additional info of a proposal lazy instead of before hand will improve the performance and user expirience a lot.

I will provide a PR to fix this

if you look at it, lucene-core is available, but the "path" for the analyzers-commons and analyzers-smartcn are wrong.

Based on the public central Maven, it should be :
   _ org.apache.lucene.analyzers-common changed to lucene-analyzers-common
   _ org.apache.lucene.analyzers-smartcn changed to lucene-analyzers-smartcn

which are then accessible and resolved.

for now, out of the box, you receive simply 

Failed to collect dependencies at org.eclipse.platform:org.eclipse.help.base:jar:4.3.0 -> org.apache.lucene:org.apache.lucene.analyzers-common:jar:[8.4.1,9.0.0): No versions available for org.apache.lucene:org.apache.lucene.analyzers-common:jar:[8.4.1,9.0.0) within specified range

7498217498122 URL = https://bugs.eclipse.org/bugs/show_bug.cgi?id=569656

Validation of xhtml files is very slow if you have a lot of projects with a lot of managed beans. We see validation times of several minutes.

This is because JDT type resolving (IType.resolveType) is used which is slow. 

Moreover the same type is resolved over and over again for the same managed bean. To create a IBeanPropertySymbol the type of the property gets resolved 4 times.
If a bean has 6 String properties. The type String is resolved 4 x 6 = 24 times.
The same is true for methods. Here the return type and a parameter types are resolved. 

Also annotations on managed beans are resolved multiple times. And annotions like @SuppressWarning gets resolved even it is clear that it has nothing to do with JSF.

This can be improved a lot by caching resolved types for each bean type. 
The validation time will be reduced to around 25% by doing so. 

I will provide a PR that will implement this.

7498217498122 URL = https://bugs.eclipse.org/bugs/show_bug.cgi?id=569551

The ImageLoader class is using the GDK.gdk_pixbuf_save_to_bufferv method to save images, but is passing null for the option_keys and option_values attributes, so the compression attribute is ignored.

Accoding to the GDK documentation, for JPEG images it should pass the string "quality" in option_keys and a value in the range [0,100] in option_values. For PNG images it should pass the string "compression" in option_keys and an integer in the range of [0,9] in option_values.

7498217498122 URL = https://bugs.eclipse.org/bugs/show_bug.cgi?id=569616

When I call a generics method from within a stream I might need a cast. But Eclipse thinks it doesn't and so it suggests to remove the cast. Following this advice will lead to a compile error.

If I have the code

public class GenericsCast {

	public static void main(String[] args) throws Exception {
		Set<String> input = Set.of("1", "2", "3");
		Set<Foo> result = createFoos(input);
		System.out.println(result);
	}

	private static Set<Foo> createFoos(Set<String> input) {
		return input.stream().map(s -> {
			return (Foo) createFoo(s); // <== Warning
		}).collect(Collectors.toSet());
	}

	static class Foo {

		public final String s;

		public Foo(String s) {
			this.s = s;
		}
	}

	static <E extends Foo> E createFoo(String s) {
		@SuppressWarnings("unchecked")
		E result = (E) new Foo(s);
		return result;
	}
}

then Eclipse will show me a warning "Unnecessary cast from GenericsCast.Foo to GenericsCast.Foo".

The quickfix will then change the method to

        private static Set<Foo> createFoos(Set<String> input) {
		return input.stream().map(s -> { // <== Error
			return createFoo(s);
		}).collect(Collectors.toSet());
	}

which will show an error "Type mismatch: cannot convert from Set<Object> to Set<GenericsCast.Foo>".

I'm not entirely sure where the problem is, but note that

	private static Set<Foo> createFoos(Set<String> input) {
		return input.stream().map(s -> {
			Foo foo = createFoo(s);
			return foo;
		}).collect(Collectors.toSet());
	}

works fine.

7498217498122 URL = https://bugs.eclipse.org/bugs/show_bug.cgi?id=569561

Dual monitors with differing DPI: small monitor is 96dpi, and large is 48dpi...

THIS IS NOT a twinview configuration.  It is a distinct DISPLAY for each physical monitor.

Xresource file properly specified the following:

! screen 0 resources
#if SCREEN_NUM == 0
*Xft.dpi:       96
#endif

! screen 1 resources
#if SCREEN_NUM == 1
*Xft.dpi:       48
#endif

yet eclipse IDE GUI does not process the correct Xft.dpi value.

However, manually forcing the resource as follows:

echo "*Xft.dpi: 48" | xrdb -merge -

and then running eclipse only half fixes the problem because then BOTH monitors are using the 48dpi value.  which breaks the scaling on the secondary monitor...Either Java or eclipse itself is NOT processing the X resources correctly from the resource database in dual-screen mode.


I do NOT use gnome, kde, or any other other bloated desktop environments.  This  X11 running openbox on each display.

7498217498122 URL = https://bugs.eclipse.org/bugs/show_bug.cgi?id=569271

According to

https://docs.oracle.com/javase/specs/jls/se7/html/jls-17.html#jls-17.5

For the programm

class FinalFieldExample {
    final int x;
    int y;
    static FinalFieldExample f;

    public FinalFieldExample() {
        x = 3;
        y = 4;
    }

    static void writer() {
        f = new FinalFieldExample();
    }

    static void reader() {
        if (f != null) {
            int i = f.x;  // guaranteed to see 3
            int j = f.y;  // could see 0
        }
    }
}

only on a final field the initialization is given to be seen by other
threads.
While it is not an always an issue the question is if it makes sense to
use final where possible anyway.

http://www.cs.umd.edu/~pugh/java/memoryModel/jsr-133-faq.html#finalWrong
https://stackoverflow.com/questions/22743223/are-final-fields-really-useful-regarding-thread-safety

Issue:  TLS cookie without secure flag set
Severity: Medium
Confidence:  Firm
Host:  https://help.eclipse.org
  
Issue detail
10 instances of this issue were identified.
The following cookie was received:

JSESSIONID
  
Issue background

If the secure flag is set on a cookie, then browsers will not submit the cookie in any requests that use an unencrypted HTTP connection, thereby preventing the cookie from being trivially intercepted by an attacker monitoring network traffic. If the secure flag is not set, then the cookie will be transmitted in clear-text if the user visits any HTTP URLs within the cookie's scope. An attacker may be able to induce this event by feeding a user suitable links, either directly or via another web site. Even if the domain that issued the cookie does not host any content that is accessed over HTTP, an attacker may be able to use links of the form http://example.com:443/ to perform the same attack.
To exploit this vulnerability, an attacker must be suitably positioned to eavesdrop on the victim's network traffic. This scenario typically occurs when a client communicates with the server over an insecure connection such as public Wi-Fi, or a corporate or home network that is shared with a compromised computer. Common defenses such as switched networks are not sufficient to prevent this. An attacker situated in the user's ISP or the application's hosting infrastructure could also perform this attack. Note that an advanced adversary could potentially target any connection made over the Internet's core infrastructure.

Issue remediation

The secure flag should be set on all cookies that are used for transmitting sensitive data when accessing content over HTTPS. If cookies are used to transmit session tokens, then areas of the application that are accessed over HTTPS should employ their own session handling mechanism, and the session tokens used should never be transmitted over unencrypted communications.

Vulnerability classifications

CWE-614: Sensitive Cookie in HTTPS Session Without 'Secure' Attribute
https://cwe.mitre.org/data/definitions/614.html







Issue:  Cookie without HttpOnly flag set
Severity:  Low
Confidence: Firm
Host: https://help.eclipse.org
  
Issue detail
10 instances of this issue were identified. The following cookie was received:

JSESSIONID
  
Issue background

If the HttpOnly attribute is set on a cookie, then the cookie's value cannot be read or set by client-side JavaScript. This measure makes certain client-side attacks, such as cross-site scripting, slightly harder to exploit by preventing them from trivially capturing the cookie's value via an injected script.

Issue remediation

There is usually no good reason not to set the HttpOnly flag on all cookies. Unless you specifically require legitimate client-side scripts within your application to read or set a cookie's value, you should set the HttpOnly flag by including this attribute within the relevant Set-cookie directive.
You should be aware that the restrictions imposed by the HttpOnly flag can potentially be circumvented in some circumstances, and that numerous other serious attacks can be delivered by client-side script injection, aside from simple cookie stealing.

References Configuring HttpOnly
https://owasp.org/www-community/HttpOnly

Vulnerability classifications
CWE-16: Configuration
https://cwe.mitre.org/data/definitions/16.html

7498217498122 URL = https://bugs.eclipse.org/bugs/show_bug.cgi?id=568952

In an IDE that *only* has Java 11 configured
Create a PDE plugin project that has JavaSE-1.8 as BREE.
Project references the Java 11 install as JRE (there is no other one).
Add `Import-Package: javax.annotation`
Check classpath: javax.annotation is not part of Resolved Dependencies. The reason seems to be that despite Java 11 is actually configured as JRE for the project, PDE uses that package list from JavaSE-1.8 (taken from a .profile most probably) to do the resolution and assume the package comes from the JRE.
It would be more convenient that PDE resolves dependencies against the *actual* configured JRE instead of against the BREE, as we don't have guarantee of a perfect match in the IDE.

7498217498122 URL = https://bugs.eclipse.org/bugs/show_bug.cgi?id=569383

I would like a text widget that selects all of its text when it gains focus. 
This doesn't appear to be currently supported by SWT.

1.) Run snippet
2.) Select left text box with the mouse.


OBSERVED RESULTS:
Selection expands to all of the text, and then reduces to just the cursor.


DESIRED RESULTS:
Selection expands to all of the text, and stays that way.



I have to wrap it into a display.asyncExec(() -> text.setSelection(0, text.getText().length()))

This seems to be the same issue as Bug 46059 which got marked as fixed but it still does not work.

----

/*
 * Text example snippet: implement content assist
 *
 * For a list of all SWT example snippets see
 * http://www.eclipse.org/swt/snippets/
 */
import org.eclipse.swt.SWT;
import org.eclipse.swt.layout.GridData;
import org.eclipse.swt.layout.GridLayout;
import org.eclipse.swt.widgets.Display;
import org.eclipse.swt.widgets.Shell;
import org.eclipse.swt.widgets.Text;

public class Snippet320 {

	private static Text text;

public static void main(String [] args) {
	final Display display = new Display();
	final Shell shell = new Shell(display);
	shell.setText("Snippet 320");
	shell.setLayout(new GridLayout());
	Text local = new Text(shell, SWT.SINGLE | SWT.BORDER);
	text = new Text(shell, SWT.SINGLE | SWT.BORDER);
	// This does not work
	text.addListener(SWT.FocusIn, event -> text.selectAll());
	// This does work
//	text.addListener(SWT.FocusIn, event -> display.asyncExec(() -> text.setSelection(0, text.getText().length())));
	text.setLayoutData(new GridData(150, SWT.DEFAULT));
	shell.pack();
	shell.open();



	while (!shell.isDisposed()) {
		if (!display.readAndDispatch()) display.sleep();
	}
	display.dispose();
}

}

7498217498122 URL = https://bugs.eclipse.org/bugs/show_bug.cgi?id=569685

I was recently trying to use the swtbot.swt.finder keyboard functionality in our automatic testsuite for a DE_DE keyboard layout and observed, that the existing keyboard support for basically every provided keyboard except EN-boards is broken. My first thought was that this is caused by the incomplete DE_DE.keyboard file (There are some obvious key combinations missing, but I will open a separate issue for this), but unfortunately this turned not out to be the actual reason (because that could have been fixed completely on my end by providing a fixed DE_DE.keyboard via the SWTBotPreferences customization points as described in https://wiki.eclipse.org/SWTBot/Keyboard_Layouts).

Further analysis revealed that _all_ key combinations that require more than one modifier key (one of ALT, CTRL, SHIFT, or COMMAND) are not properly translated, _regardless_ of the the actual keyboard and also regardless of the KeyboardStrategy used. For example, on a DE_DE layout for producing the character { you need the key combination ALT+CTRL+7. Using org.eclipse.swtbot.swt.finder.keyboard.Keyboard#typeText on the String "{" doesn't type "{", but types "27" instead. Since the file org/eclipse/swtbot/swt/finder/keyboard/DE_DE.keyboard _does_ contain this necessary mapping, the file wasn't the root of this particular problem. The cause of this problem is located in org.eclipse.swtbot.swt.finder.keyboard.Keystrokes#create(char) method (and to some lesser extend in org.eclipse.swtbot.swt.finder.keyboard.Keystrokes.toKeys(int modificationKeys, char c)). The reason for the problem in create is that this method doesn't produce _individual_ KeyStroke elements for _each_ individual modifier out of which KeyStroke.getModifierKeys() is composed of: If at least one modifier is part of a character KeyStroke, only a single modifier KeyStroke is produced that represents _all_ contributing modifier keys:
```
public static KeyStroke[] create(char ch) {
	KeyStroke keyStroke = defaultKeyboardLayout.keyStrokeFor(ch);
	if (keyStroke.getModifierKeys() == KeyStroke.NO_KEY)
		return new KeyStroke[] { keyStroke };
	KeyStroke modifier = KeyStroke.getInstance(keyStroke.getModifierKeys(), 0);
	KeyStroke key = KeyStroke.getInstance(0, keyStroke.getNaturalKey());
	return new KeyStroke[] { modifier, key };
}
```
When this insufficiently decomposed KeyStroke sequence is send to the actual KeyboardStrategy#pressKeys method, the modifier part is not properly understood. For example for SWTKeyboardStrategy this is handed over to org.eclipse.swt.widgets.Display.post(Event event) whose internal untranslateKey doesn't find an appropriate virtual key (understandably, because there exists no such single virtual key), and the OS.VkKeyScan call return 50 (corresponding to character '2') for the virtual keycode for character '\0', resulting in the observed nonsense.
The right fix seems to be that above Keystrokes#create(char) should decompose the modifier parts correctly, very similar to the way the existing method toKeys(int modificationKeys, char c) does it in its "modificationKeys != 0" branch. This brings me to the minor problem in that very same method as well: Albeit Keystrokes.toKeys(int modificationKeys, char c) has a correct "modificationKeys != 0"  branch, this method also delegates 
Keystrokes.create(char ch) at the very end and ignores here possible modifiers of the character itself. So albeit we could fix Keystrokes#create(char) alone by something similar to
```
public static KeyStroke[] create(char ch) {
	final KeyStroke keyStroke = keyStrokeFor(ch);
	final int key = keyStroke.getNaturalKey();
	final int modificationKeys = keyStroke.getModifierKeys();
	if (modificationKeys == KeyStroke.NO_KEY && key != KeyStroke.NO_KEY)
		return new KeyStroke[] { keyStroke };
	final LinkedHashSet<KeyStroke> keys = new LinkedHashSet<>();
	final int[] sortModifierKeys = sortModifierKeys(modificationKeys);
	for (int modifierKey : sortModifierKeys) {
		if (modifierKey != KeyStroke.NO_KEY)
			keys.add(KeyStroke.getInstance(modifierKey, KeyStroke.NO_KEY));
	}
	if (key != KeyStroke.NO_KEY)
		keys.add(KeyStroke.getInstance(KeyStroke.NO_KEY, key));
	return keys.toArray(new KeyStroke[keys.size()]);
}
```
my personal suggestion would be to fix _both_ Keystrokes#create(char) and Keystrokes#toKeys(int modificationKeys, char c), e.g. as follows. First fix toKeys to be the more general case:
```
public static KeyStroke[] toKeys(int modificationKeys, char c) {
	final KeyStroke keyStroke = keyStrokeFor(c);
	final int key = keyStroke.getNaturalKey();
	final int modifications = keyStroke.getModifierKeys() | modificationKeys;
	if (modifications == KeyStroke.NO_KEY && key != KeyStroke.NO_KEY)
		return new KeyStroke[] { keyStroke };
	final LinkedHashSet<KeyStroke> keys = new LinkedHashSet<>();
	final int[] sortModifierKeys = sortModifierKeys(modifications);
	for (int modifierKey : sortModifierKeys) {
		if (modifierKey != KeyStroke.NO_KEY)
			keys.add(KeyStroke.getInstance(modifierKey, KeyStroke.NO_KEY));
	}
	if (key != KeyStroke.NO_KEY)
		keys.add(KeyStroke.getInstance(KeyStroke.NO_KEY, key));
	return keys.toArray(new KeyStroke[keys.size()]);
}
```
and then define Keystrokes#create(char) in terms of that method:
```
public static KeyStroke[] create(char ch) {
	return toKeys(KeyStroke.NO_KEY, ch);
}
```
I tested both variants and both fix the problem for me.

7498217498122 URL = https://bugs.eclipse.org/bugs/show_bug.cgi?id=569038

At least in two testsuites instability was caused by premature garbage collection of instances created with ContextInjectionFactory.make, see Bug 551744 and Bug 566172. By default, instances created with this factory are only referenced by weak references in the context. Therefore they can be garbage collected at any time, resulting in unexpected behavior. This can also happen in production code.

Correct ownership of these instances must be validated. There are different strategies used now:
1. The caller of ContextInjectionFactory.make has a field reference to the result
2. The caller of ContextInjectionFactory.make adds the result to the context
3. The @PostConstruct method in the instance created adds itself to the context
4. No (non-weak) reference to the instance.

The 4th strategy was the root cause of the bugs mentioned above.

To me, the first two strategies or correct. The 3rd feels as if control is reverted, and therefore a any-pattern. The 4th should not be used, unless the instance is never to be referenced.
All code should be reviewed on the use of this factory. Also, the documentation of ContextInjectionFactory.make could be made more clear to emphasize that the created instance is not (non-weak) referenced.

7498217498122 URL = https://bugs.eclipse.org/bugs/show_bug.cgi?id=569472

look at https://help.eclipse.org/2020-09/index.jsp

This issue is *not* about the content of the eclipse help but about the implementation of the infocenter server.

Issue:  Cacheable HTTPS response
Severity:  Information
Confidence: Certain
Host:  https://help.eclipse.org
  
Issue detail
5 instances of this issue were identified, at the following locations:
/2020-09/advanced/content.jsp
/2020-09/advanced/help.jsp
/2020-09/advanced/helpToolbar.jsp
/2020-09/advanced/nav.jsp
/2020-09/advanced/search.jsp
  
Issue background

Unless directed otherwise, browsers may store a local cached copy of content received from web servers. Some browsers, including Internet Explorer, cache content accessed via HTTPS. If sensitive information in application responses is stored in the local cache, then this may be retrieved by other users who have access to the same computer at a future time.

Issue remediation

Applications should return caching directives instructing browsers not to store local copies of any sensitive data. Often, this can be achieved by configuring the web server to prevent caching for relevant paths within the web root. Alternatively, most web development platforms allow you to control the server's caching directives from within individual scripts. Ideally, the web server should return the following HTTP headers in all responses containing sensitive content:

Cache-control: no-store
Pragma: no-cache

Vulnerability classifications
CWE-524: Information Exposure Through Caching
CWE-525: Information Exposure Through Browser Caching

7498217498122 URL = https://bugs.eclipse.org/bugs/show_bug.cgi?id=569476

This is about infocenter implementation.

A request like this:

GET /2020-09/topic/org.eclipse.wb.doc.user/html/index.html?cp=94 HTTP/1.1
Host: help.eclipse.org

is responded like this

HTTP/1.1 200 OK
Server: nginx
Date: Fri, 04 Dec 2020 15:51:47 GMT
Content-Type: text/html
Connection: close
Vary: Accept-Encoding
Cache-Control: max-age=86400
Expires: Sat, 05 Dec 2020 15:51:47 GMT
Strict-Transport-Security: max-age=15552000; includeSubDomains; preload
X-Frame-Options: SAMEORIGIN
X-Content-Type-Options: nosniff
X-XSS-Protection: 1; mode=block
X-Proxy-Cache: MISS
Content-Length: 5293

Instead of 

Content-Type: text/html

It should return

Content-Type: text/html;charset=utf-8

or similar

Issue:  HTML does not specify charset
Severity: Information
Confidence: Certain
Host:  https://help.eclipse.org
  
Issue detail
4 instances of this issue were identified, at the following locations:
/2020-09/topic/org.eclipse.wb.doc.user/html/index.html
/2020-09/topic/org.eclipse.wb.doc.user/html/installation/index.html
/2020-09/topic/org.eclipse.wb.doc.user/html/quick_start.html
/2020-09/topic/org.eclipse.wb.doc.user/html/userinterface/index.html
  
Issue background

If a response states that it contains HTML content but does not specify a character set, then the browser may analyze the HTML and attempt to determine which character set it appears to be using. Even if the majority of the HTML actually employs a standard character set such as UTF-8, the presence of non-standard characters anywhere in the response may cause the browser to interpret the content using a different character set. This can have unexpected results, and can lead to cross-site scripting vulnerabilities in which non-standard encodings like UTF-7 can be used to bypass the application's defensive filters.
In most cases, the absence of a charset directive does not constitute a security flaw, particularly if the response contains static content. You should review the contents of affected responses, and the context in which they appear, to determine whether any vulnerability exists.

Issue remediation

For every response containing HTML content, the application should include within the Content-type header a directive specifying a standard recognized character set, for example charset=ISO-8859-1.

Vulnerability classifications
CWE-16: Configuration
CWE-436: Interpretation Conflict

https://cwe.mitre.org/data/definitions/16.html
https://cwe.mitre.org/data/definitions/436.html

7498217498122 URL = https://bugs.eclipse.org/bugs/show_bug.cgi?id=569560

I believe the integrated Jetty web server uses a tcp port to host the documentation, and binds that port to a network interface.

7498217498122 URL = https://bugs.eclipse.org/bugs/show_bug.cgi?id=569657



7498217498122 URL = https://bugs.eclipse.org/bugs/show_bug.cgi?id=569633

Created attachment 285016 [details]
threaddump

I see sporadic OsgiManifestParserException and ZipExceptions in our parallel build with a tycho 2.2.0 snapshot when building against an empty .m2 directory.

Both exceptions are caused by empty jar files in .m2/p2/osgi/bundle. I believe they are caused by a race condition in MirroringArtifactRepository::makeOneFormatLocallyAvailable:

        if (localArtifactRepository.contains(key)) {
            return true;
        } else if (remoteProviders.contains(key)) {
            downloadArtifact(key);
            return true;
        } else {
            return false;
        }

Multiple resolver threads may enter at the same time and all download that artifact in parallel. Or as in the attached threaddump, one thread downloads and tries to read the file while another then starts its own download, overwriting it.

I think this issue only surfaced with the delayed artifact download, because earlier there was a checkpoint were all downloads were finished before anyone would try to read the downloaded files.

I don't have solution quite yet, but I think we should make the parallel resolving opt-in until it is more stable.

7498217498122 URL = https://bugs.eclipse.org/bugs/show_bug.cgi?id=569384

The steps of document generation are currently not undoable. The goal of this bug it to provide an undo for each of this step.
The concerned steps are:
  1. Document structure generation from Document template
  2. Document (odt or docx) generation from Document structure
  3. Document structure AND document (docx or odt) generation in one step from a Document template
  4. Document structure AND document (docx or odt) AND PDF generation in one step from a Document template
  5. document (docx or odt) AND PDF generation in one step from a Document Structure
     
The undo will consist in destroying generated files, so we won't distinguish a pre-existing file modified by a new generation process and a file newly created.
Here we will only manage files generated into the Eclipse workspace. 
Files generated outside of Eclipse will be ignored.
The created folders won't be destroyed by this undo.

7498217498122 URL = https://bugs.eclipse.org/bugs/show_bug.cgi?id=569108

Hi,

I deactivated some views using activity patterns. Although I can't open them the ShowViewsDialog lists the disabled views.

I found the problem in the ContentProvider of the TreeViewer.

ViewContentProvider#isFilteredByActivity checks whether the given view id is filtered. However, it uses  viewRegistry.getViews() to find the view for the given id. getViews() is already filtering out disabled views, therefore the content provider can't find the view with the id to check and defaults to "unfiltered".

I see two solutions:
Either extend isFilteredByActivity so it also returns true if the view wasn't found or use the viewRegistry in the methods determineTopLevelElements and determineViewsInCategory instead of application.getDescriptors().

7498217498122 URL = https://bugs.eclipse.org/bugs/show_bug.cgi?id=569107

Designer prefixes parameter type declarations in the header file with "struct", but not in the body. This is not a problem for generated types for which a type A is declared as "typedef struct A A;". However, the assumption that the typedef points to an element of the same name does not hold for external types and inconsistent type declarations are reported by the compiler.

Due to the typedef declaration in the header files, prefixing types in header files with "struct" is not necessary and should be removed.

7498217498122 URL = https://bugs.eclipse.org/bugs/show_bug.cgi?id=569223

Created attachment 284904 [details]
Example Maven project to reproduce the issue (path2gc-bug.zip)

Environment
===========
- AdoptOpenJDK jdk8u272-b10
- Apache Tomcat 8.5.59
- Maven 3.6.0

Use case
========
A Tomcat web application has a class loader leak during undeployment. Eclipse MAT shall be used to identify this leak.

Steps to reproduce
==================
1. Build attached Maven project path2gc-bug.zip (mvn clean install).
2. Deploy the .war file (web application) into running Tomcat.
3. Undeploy the web application again.
4. Acquire a heap dump with Eclipse MAT.
5. Identify the ParallelWebappClassLoader instance of the undeployed application (state == DESTROYED).
6. Determine the Path To GC Root (exclude weak references) of the ParallelWebappClassLoader.

Expected result
===============
There should be only one Path To GC Root, leading to java.util.ResourceBundle.cacheList.

Actual result
=============
There is also a Path To GC Root to the <resolved_references> of a java.lang.invoke.LambdaForm$DMH class (see ClassLoader_path2GC.png). I think this is wrong and confusing. The class is no GC root, it is rather retained by the ParallelWebappClassLoader (see LambdaForm_incoming.png). When removing the ResourceBundle creation from the code, the ParallelWebappClassLoader can be GCed (it only needs one more cycle).

7498217498122 URL = https://bugs.eclipse.org/bugs/show_bug.cgi?id=569478

This is about infocenter implementation. Maybe the easiest is to add a referer-policy.

Issue:  Cross-domain Referer leakage
Severity:  Information
Confidence:  Certain
Host:  https://help.eclipse.org
Path:  /2020-09/topic/org.eclipse.jdt.doc.user/whatsNew/jdt_whatsnew.html
  
Issue detail

The page was loaded from a URL containing a query string:
https://help.eclipse.org/2020-09/topic/org.eclipse.jdt.doc.user/whatsNew/jdt_whatsnew.html

The response contains the following link to another domain:
https://openjdk.java.net/jeps/358
  
Issue background

When a web browser makes a request for a resource, it typically adds an HTTP header, called the "Referer" header, indicating the URL of the resource from which the request originated. This occurs in numerous situations, for example when a web page loads an image or script, or when a user clicks on a link or submits a form.
If the resource being requested resides on a different domain, then the Referer header is still generally included in the cross-domain request. If the originating URL contains any sensitive information within its query string, such as a session token, then this information will be transmitted to the other domain. If the other domain is not fully trusted by the application, then this may lead to a security compromise.
You should review the contents of the information being transmitted to other domains, and also determine whether those domains are fully trusted by the originating application.
Today's browsers may withhold the Referer header in some situations (for example, when loading a non-HTTPS resource from a page that was loaded over HTTPS, or when a Refresh directive is issued), but this behavior should not be relied upon to protect the originating URL from disclosure.
Note also that if users can author content within the application then an attacker may be able to inject links referring to a domain they control in order to capture data from URLs used within the application.

Issue remediation

Applications should never transmit any sensitive information within the URL query string. In addition to being leaked in the Referer header, such information may be logged in various locations and may be visible on-screen to untrusted parties. If placing sensitive information in the URL is unavoidable, consider using the Referer-Policy HTTP header to reduce the chance of it being disclosed to third parties.

References
Referer Policy
https://developer.mozilla.org/en-US/docs/Web/HTTP/Headers/Referrer-Policy

Vulnerability classifications
CWE-200: Information Exposure
https://cwe.mitre.org/data/definitions/200.html

Last week one of my customers pointed out how bad the Eclipse Find / Replace dialog is compared to tools like VSCode.

In Eclipse you have to move the cursor or search backwards (listing again all the previous results) to find matches above the current cursor position.

7498217498122 URL = https://bugs.eclipse.org/bugs/show_bug.cgi?id=569590

Platform uses a number of times simple accessor instead of the double-check idiom for instance fields with lazy initialization. Simple accessor is not thread safe.

If you need high-performance lazy initializing of an instance field, use
the double-check idiom with a volatile field. This idiom wasn't
guaranteed to work until release 5.0, when the platform got a new memory
model. The idiom is very fast but also complicated and delicate, so
don't be tempted to modify it in any way. Just copy and paste --
normally not a good idea, but appropriate here:

// Double-check idiom for lazy initialization of instance fields.
private volatile FieldType field;
FieldType getField() {
    FieldType result = field;
    if (result == null) { // First check (no locking)
        synchronized(this) {
            result = field;
            if (result == null) // Second check (with locking)
                field = result = computeFieldValue();
        }
    }
     return result;
}

see https://www.oracle.com/technical-resources/articles/javase/bloch-effective-08-qa.html

http://www.cs.umd.edu/~pugh/java/memoryModel/DoubleCheckedLocking.html

7498217498122 URL = https://bugs.eclipse.org/bugs/show_bug.cgi?id=569614

The relevant features are Records and Instanceof pattern

7498217498122 URL = https://bugs.eclipse.org/bugs/show_bug.cgi?id=569665

Hi,

since version 15, the OpenJDK VM (and all derived from it) has an option to directly create a gzipped hrpof dump via a the GC.heap_dummp jcmd. Since the gzip algorithm is not particularly fast, it uses mutliple threads to do the compression in parallel. This leads to a gzip file which contains more than one "member" (see the section 2.2 and 2.3 of the gzip RFC at https://tools.ietf.org/html/rfc1952).

This should pose no problem, but MAT does not handle such a file correctly for two reasons. First, it tries to look at the end of the gzip file to determine the original size (modulo 4G). But if the file contains more than one "member", you only get the size of the last "member". The more important problem is that the GZipInputStream2 does not handle multiple "members" at all. Since for the initial parsing the code uses the GzipInputStream from the JDK (which handles this correctly) you don't directly see problems. But when using the HprofRandomAccessParser in an analysis, problems occur if the object is not in the first "member".

Additionally this multi-"member" format can be used as an advantage, since you can start reading at every start of a "member". Since the uncompessed size of a "member" created by the OpenJDK is 1 MB at most, this can be used to have a relative inexpensive random access mode, without having to decompress it beforehand. The OpenJDK adds a comment in the first "member" which specifies the maximum uncompressed size of a "member" (called chunk from now on). Using the value from the comment one can easily identify such a file and can create a mapping which allows to efficiently find the file position you have to read to get the data for a specific uncompressed position. This can be done during the initial parsing, where we read the file from from front to back.

I've implemented this by adding a new RandomAccessFile version called ChunkedGZIPRandomAccessFile. It has code to detect if the file is in the specific format. The BufferingRafPositionInputStream will then use this class when it detects that format. Since MAT creates several random access files during the analysis, the file position to logical position mapping of a file is remembered, so it doesn't has to be recreated for every RandomAccessFile object for the same file. This needs some memory, so the storage format is efficient (8 bytes per chunk, so 8kb per 1GB uncompressed hprof file in the case of the OpenJDK with 1 MB chunks) and the number of stored mappings is limited. Additionally each instance of the  ChunkedGZIPRandomAccessFile maintains a small cache for already read data (currently 5 MB). Comparing that to GZipInputStream2, which needs to store the dictionary for every position you want to start decompressing from, it uses much less memory (e.g. for a 8BG compressed hprof file the new code used about 10 MB and the old one about 500 MB).

When testing the code I found a bug in Pass1Parser.checkSkipBytes(), which does not handle skips > 2GB (since the size of the hprof entries are unsigned 32 values, this can happen). The fix for this is inlcuded in the patch I will propose.

I tried to keep the needed code mostly in the new ChunkedGZIPRandomAccessFile class, but some small changed to some already existing classes had to be done. To test the code with a unit test, I added the option (not accessible via the UI) to create a gzipped compressed heap dump in the same format that OpenJDK 15+ would create.

Best regards,
Ralf Schmelter

GOT => editor for longFileName_forALongTab7.txt maximized

Edited from: https://www.eclipse.org/lists/tycho-user/msg08751.html

I am seeing similar problems that at first sight seemed magical; Java works interactively but not on Jenkins.

I was doing a six month catchup so moving from

Java 8 to Java 11
Eclipse 4.16 to 4.18
Tycho 1.4.0 to 2.1.0
Maven 3.0 to 3.6.3
vintage to modern Maven tool versions

After permuting the changes, I eventually found that the only significant and solid difference between old-working and new-broken was the Tycho version.

Somehow Tycho 2.1.0 disrupts the Java compiler activation so that the non-null flow analysis forgets that something is not-null within an if guard or after an assert. But probably not universally since I only get a few rather than hundreds of errors as a result. Possibly something magic has happened to the external annotations path. But ...

https://ci.eclipse.org/ocl/job/ocl-branch-tests/228/console shows the two spurious compiler errors.

Tycho 1.6.0 seems ok.

Tycho 1.7.0, 2.0.0 seems to have an intermediate condition whereby many, often bogus, non-check warnings are reported as errors breaking the build.

It would seem that the compiler invocation is somehow broken. If someone can suggest some debug settings to cause the compiler invocation to be logged verbosely, it may prove quite easy to find the problem.

For now, Tycho > 1.6 is not fit for Eclipse OCL build purposes.
