7498217498122 URL = https://bugs.eclipse.org/bugs/show_bug.cgi?id=569239



7498217498122 URL = https://bugs.eclipse.org/bugs/show_bug.cgi?id=569679

Eclipse OCL is installable from Oxygen onwards and is tested as such. Consequently the MANIFEST.MF BREEs must be compatible with Oxygen - typically BREE 8.

However in order to develop code and detect paltform deprecations it is necessary to use Java 11 and a recent platform for development.

Consequently every MANIFEST.MF has a 

"One of the plug-in's dependencies requires an execution environment of JavaSE-11, hence this plug-in's execution environment should be at least JavaSE-11."

This is not true. The lowerbound of the dependencies accommodates Oxygen and so the plugin's declared dependencies require only what the transitive lowerbound mandates, not what the target platform happens to provide. (Just the same as specifying Java 5 class compatibility is quite acceptable with a Java 11 compiler.) 

Either the "warning" should be at most an "info", or the manifest editor should offer a separate stronger slower Validate action that uses the transitive lowerbounds to use the actual transitive dependencies of plugins to give a truthful diagnostic.

7498217498122 URL = https://bugs.eclipse.org/bugs/show_bug.cgi?id=569273

This Bug split off from Bug 564265 to localize the discussion.

Developing a declarative serializer highlights a strange characteristic of the Xtext grammar.

This is clearly seen by the 'explanatory' comments in AbstractTerminal

  // Keyword and RuleCall are used inside of Assignable terminal
  // As we do not want to be able to write name==>ID
  // the rules for Keyword and RuleCall have been copied
	
  // We have to make this one explicit since the ParenthesizedElement does not
  // create an object but we have to set the predicated flag

The declarative serializer creates serialization rules from the parser rules. Serialization rules are similar to but simpler than parser rules. No actions, Alternatives only at root / leaves. Consequently for each user type there are a small number of alternative serialization rules that produce precisely the user element class, and an even smaller number that are containment compatible. There are also no unassigned serialization rule calls since all such calls are flattened.

Flattening the Alternatives grammar rule to determine the equivalent serialzation rules gives:

Alternatives returns AbstractElement:
	{Assignment} feature=ValidID operator=('+='|'='|'?=') ^terminal=AssignableTerminal cardinality=('?'|'*'|'+')?
|	{Assignment} predicated?='=>' feature=ValidID operator=('+='|'='|'?=') ^terminal=AssignableTerminal cardinality=('?'|'*'|'+')?
|	{Assignment} firstSetPredicated?='->' feature=ValidID operator=('+='|'='|'?=') ^terminal=AssignableTerminal cardinality=('?'|'*'|'+')?
|	{Keyword} value=STRING cardinality=('?'|'*'|'+')?
|	{Keyword} predicated?='=>' value=STRING cardinality=('?'|'*'|'+')?
|	{Keyword} firstSetPredicated?='->' value=STRING cardinality=('?'|'*'|'+')?
|	{RuleCall} rule=[AbstractRule|RuleID] ('<' arguments+=NamedArgument (',' arguments+=NamedArgument)* '>')? cardinality=('?'|'*'|'+')?
|	{RuleCall} predicated?='=>' rule=[AbstractRule|RuleID] ('<' arguments+=NamedArgument (',' arguments+=NamedArgument)* '>')? cardinality=('?'|'*'|'+')?
|	{RuleCall} firstSetPredicated?='->' rule=[AbstractRule|RuleID] ('<' arguments+=NamedArgument (',' arguments+=NamedArgument)* '>')? cardinality=('?'|'*'|'+')?
|	'(' Alternatives ')' cardinality=('?'|'*'|'+')?
|	{Action} '{' type=TypeRef ('.' feature=ValidID operator=('='|'+=') 'current')? '}'
| 	{Group} elements+=AbstractToken (elements+=AbstractToken)+
|	{Group} predicated?='=>' '(' elements+=Alternatives ')' cardinality=('?'|'*'|'+')?
|	{Group} firstSetPredicated?='->' '(' elements+=Alternatives ')' cardinality=('?'|'*'|'+')?
| 	{UnorderedGroup} elements+=Group ('&' elements+=Group)+
| 	{Group} '<' guardCondition=Disjunction '>' (elements+=AbstractToken)+
|	{Alternatives} elements+=ConditionalBranch ('|' elements+=ConditionalBranch)+
;

All but one of these produces precisely one type with assignments. However

Alternatives returns AbstractElement:
	...
|	'(' Alternatives ')' cardinality=('?'|'*'|'+')?
|	...

is recursive, causing a StackOverflow as the current serializer analysis recursively flattens,

The grammar allows the gratuitously parenthesized and ambiguously cardinality'd ((((Y)?)+))*

The ambiguity is trapped by a validation rule.

-----

Xtext issue:

I suspect that the grammar problem would go away if there was a sensible:

ParenthesizedCompoundElement returns AbstractElement:
     {Group} '(' elements+=AbstractToken* ')'
|    {Alternatives} '(' elements+=ConditionalBranch ('|' elements+=ConditionalBranch)+ ')'

or, if the gratuitous parentheses are needed for compatibility:

ParenthesizedCompoundElement returns AbstractElement:
     '(' AbstractToken ')'
|    {Group} '(' elements+=AbstractToken elements+=AbstractToken+ ')'
|    {Alternatives} '(' elements+=ConditionalBranch ('|' elements+=ConditionalBranch)+ ')'

(Incidentally AbstractTokenWithCardinality/AbstractToken are confusing since AbstractToken has a cardinality.)

-----

Serializer analysis issue:

The troublesome Alternatives recursion cannot be flattened.

Introducing an UnassignedRuleCallSerializationNode for what cannot be flattened appesrs to solve the problem, but just creates a new one. The serializer expects to use the EClass-relvant rules and check their slots to choose the rule. The inner UnassignedRuleCallSerializationNode will choose a rule and check its slots before the outer rule assigns and checks the same slots again. The inner check is liable to fail since not all slots have been used.

Examining '(' Alternatives ')' cardinality=('?'|'*'|'+')? more carefully, it is semi-redundant or rather ambiguous in giving the serializer a choice between X, (X), ((X)), (((X))) etc for which we obviously choose minimal X. The punctuation elements are not needed. We  just need  to be sure that any prefix/suffix assignments are respected. For the example, the cardinality=('?'|'*'|'+')? suffix must be present in all serialization rules, requiring the final three rules to double up as e.g.

| 	{Group} '<' guardCondition=Disjunction '>' (elements+=AbstractToken)+
|	{Group} '(' '<' guardCondition=Disjunction '>' (elements+=AbstractToken)+')' cardinality=('?'|'*'|'+')

with a non-optional cardinality.

Pathological case: if the suffix is a many-feature assigned one at a time,
    X: ... | '(' X ')' v+=V
a five valued {v1,v2,v3,v4,v5} serialization might need to be (((((X) v1) v2) v3) v4) v5

Maybe an inner UnassignedRuleCallSerializationNode is unavoidable - must defer slot consumption compatibility to the outer node.

}

This integration will take place in several steps:
  1. Integration of the gmf tooling plugin in papyrus
  2. modification of gmf templates used in the generation to get less code generated (dead code, creation of new abstract classes,/interface...)
  3. merge this framework with the Papyrus org.eclipse.papyrus.gmfgenextension (and org.eclipse.papyrus.codegen?)
  4. merge this framework with the papyrus template Papyrus plugins : org.eclipse.papyrus.def (and org.eclipse.papyrus.codegen?)
  5. refactore metamodele to remove dependencies on GMF Tooling
  6. regenerate all existing diagrams
  
  Subtask will be created later if required to identify more easily the commits.

screenshot of change OS Display scale

If OS Display scale set to 125% or 150%, open MS Word document from eclipse File -> Open menu, word document opened externally. 

Steps to reproduce:
1. Modify System Display “Scale and Layout” to 125% or 150%. 
2. Launch eclipse4.17 (or other old version of eclipse)
3. Open TaskManager, find javaw.exe process for eclipse4.17
4. Right Mouse click on javaw.exe and select “Properties” to open Properties dialog for this process
5. From “javaw.exe Properties” dialog, go to “Compatibility” tab, and click “Change high DPI settings” button.  Check “Override high DPI scaling behavior” check box, and select “System” from dropdown list. (Please see attached screenshot)
6. Click OK to close all popped up properties dialog.
7. From ecilpse4.17, do File -> Open to open a Word file with extension “.docx”, observe that word document will be opened externally.  We are expecting word document open embedded inside eclipse4.

This problem can be reproduced with eclipse 4.10, 4.16 and 4.17. We have an RCP application that contains a Viewer, where has OLE integration that allows user to embed a MSWord document inside Viewer. With above UI display scaling settings, word document was not embedded inside Viewer, but opened externally.

There are several string based constants in NatTable that should be changed to enums for a better usability and improved API. The following classes should be considered:

- DisplayMode
This involves changing of the ILayerCell, ILayer and IConfigRegistry interfaces and respective implementations

- Mode
This involves changing ModeSupport and AbstractModeEventHandler. As these classes are mainly unsed internally, it should not affect users.

- ISearchDirection
This involves changing SearchCommand and SearchGridCellsCommandHandler and AbstractSearchStrategy.
It should be also renamed to SearchDirection to match Java naming conventions.

7498217498122 URL = https://bugs.eclipse.org/bugs/show_bug.cgi?id=569549

If a package ands with a string "xyz" and a class starts with "Xyz" before a camelcase the "Xyz" is removed in the java doc and other generated files like "plugin.properties".


For example package "test.block" and class "BlockType". The java doc will look like this ("Type" instead of "Block Type"):
//-------------------
/**
 * <!-- begin-user-doc -->
 * A representation of the model object '<em><b>Type</b></em>'.
 * <!-- end-user-doc -->
 *
 * <p>
 * The following features are supported:
 * </p>
 * <ul>
 *   <li>{@link test.block.BlockType#getName <em>Name</em>}</li>
 * </ul>
 *
 * @see test.block.BlockPackage#getBlockType()
 * @model
 * @generated
 */
public interface BlockType { 
//-------------------


Xcore Model (same effect with a ecore model):

@Ecore(nsURI="https://www.testcase.org/block")
@GenModel(modelDirectory="test/src-gen",
	complianceLevel="8.0")

package test.block

class BlockType{
	String name
}

7498217498122 URL = https://bugs.eclipse.org/bugs/show_bug.cgi?id=568906

Using 
Eclipse Web Tools Platform	
Structured Source JSON Model	
1.1.0.v201901152013	
org.eclipse.wst.json.core

When editing JSON, if "$schema" field is present, the schema is downloaded, at least when Ctrl-Space is invoked but possibly at other times, as well.

Bug: If proxy access is required for the particular installation, the class org.eclipse.wst.json.core.internal.download.HttpClientProvider
does not behave properly and does not use proxy settings even if they exist.

Using debugging I found out that at line 184 in method getProxy(HttpHost target), the proxyData.getType() is all-caps while the URL scheme is lowercase.
I am not skilled enough in Eclipse inner workings as to say why that happens but it may be perfectly normal since the proxy entries appear to be all-caps in various other places. 
Anyway, line 184 fails obviously to identify the proper proxy entry ("HTTP" != "http") and the access is finally attempted without one. And it fails.

Suggested patch:

@@ -182,7 +181,7 @@ public class HttpClientProvider {
                }
                String type = target.getSchemeName();
                for (IProxyData proxyData : select) {
-                       if (proxyData.getType().equals(type)) {
+                       if (proxyData.getType().equalsIgnoreCase(type)) {
                                return new HttpHost(proxyData.getHost(), proxyData.getPort());
                        }
                }

Thank you,
Florin

7498217498122 URL = https://bugs.eclipse.org/bugs/show_bug.cgi?id=568983

Project renaming fails for names containing non-alphanumerical characters

Scenario:
1) Create a project with name "[test]" or a variant
2) Add some elements and diagrams
3) Try to rename the .aird or .capella resource

-> Existing references towards the renamed resources are not updated


The issue comes from the use of the Word Boundary: \b in the match regex. This regex does not support non-alphanumerical characters.

For more details:
# https://docs.oracle.com/javase/tutorial/essential/regex/bounds.html
# https://www.rexegg.com/regex-boundaries.html

7498217498122 URL = https://bugs.eclipse.org/bugs/show_bug.cgi?id=569067

I get this exception often when launching layout spy from Ctrl-3 dialog. I think that the recentish changes to how that dialog works causes the regression as it created a shell, where in the past it didn't (??? not sure if that is true).

Anyway, the problem is that org.eclipse.tools.layout.spy.internal.handlers.LayoutSpyHandler.execute(ExecutionEvent) calls HandlerUtil.getActiveShell(event) but that returns the Find Actions shell, which is disposed by the time the handler is actually run, which leads to the exception below.

Note this does not fail all the time, when it does not fail the active shell returned is the (expected) main Eclipse IDE window. 

Therefore there appears to be a race condition in which org.eclipse.ui.ISources.ACTIVE_SHELL_NAME has for a short time a disposed shell in it.

Because org.eclipse.ui.ISources.ACTIVE_SHELL_NAME can have a disposed shell in it, this seems likely to affect others than just the layout spy. While we can fix this locally at layout spy by looking for disposed shell before proceeding, should it be that org.eclipse.ui.ISources.ACTIVE_SHELL_NAME can have a disposed shell?

7498217498122 URL = https://bugs.eclipse.org/bugs/show_bug.cgi?id=569439

The testcase below shows unexpected behavior with ContextInjectionFactory. When a class is created with the make method, objects will be re-injected. However, there will only be a weak reference to the created object. Therefore, the created object can be garbage collected at any time. This results in confusion for the users of this injection, see for instance Bug 569038.

Is this intended behavior? And if so, is this behavior well documented?


public class InjectTest {

	static public TestObject testObject;

	static class TestObject {
	}

	static class TestObjectReInject {
		@Inject
		public void doInject(TestObject to) {
			testObject = to;
		}
	}

	@Test
	public void testReInjectWeakRef() {
		IEclipseContext context = EclipseContextFactory.create();

		TestObject to1 = new TestObject();
		TestObject to2 = new TestObject();
		TestObject to3 = new TestObject();

		context.set(TestObject.class, to1);

		TestObjectReInject basicResult1 = ContextInjectionFactory.make(TestObjectReInject.class, context);
		assertNotNull(basicResult1);
		assertEquals(testObject, to1);

		context.set(TestObject.class, to2);
		assertEquals(testObject, to2);

		// Force garbage collection
		basicResult1 = null;
		gc();

		context.set(TestObject.class, to3);
		assertEquals(testObject, to3); // <-- FAILS
	}

	public static void gc() {
		Object obj = new Object();
		WeakReference<Object> ref = new WeakReference<>(obj);
		obj = null;
		while (ref.get() != null) {
			System.gc();
		}
	}
}

7498217498122 URL = https://bugs.eclipse.org/bugs/show_bug.cgi?id=569349

Created attachment 284930 [details]
Errors on client and server

Hi,

We are running several servers with jGit. We need to run repack from time to time to keep the repos performant. I.e. after push we test how many small packs are in the repo and when a threshold is reached we run the repack.
After upgrading jGit version we've found that if someone does the clone at the time repack is running the clone sometimes (not always) fails because the repack removes .pack file used by the clone. Server exception and client error attached.

I've tracked down the cause and it seems to be introduced between jGit 5.2 (which we upgraded from) and 5.3 and being caused by this commit: Move throw of PackInvalidException outside the catch - https://github.com/…400

The problem is that when the throw was inside of the try block the last catch block catched the exception and called openFailed(false) method. It is true that it called it with invalidate = false, which is wrong. The real problem though is that with the throw outside of the try block the openFail is not called at all and the fields activeWindows and activeCopyRawData are not set to 0. Which affects the later called tests like: if (++activeCopyRawData == 1 && activeWindows == 0).

The fix for this is relatively simple keeping the throw outside of a the try block and still having the invalid field set to true. See the attached patch (against current master). I did exhaustive testing of the change running concurrent clones and pushes indefinitely and with the patch applied it never fails where without it takes relatively short to get the error. However I'm not an expert in the jGit code and I may well be wrong about how to fix this.

7498217498122 URL = https://bugs.eclipse.org/bugs/show_bug.cgi?id=569498

When these things come together:

1. A ternary expression serves as method argument.
2. The condition or the alternatives of that ternary operator reference one or more explicitly final static or not static fields or explicitly final variables that all have their values assigned at their respective declarations.
3. All, condition and both alternatives, contain only literals or variables as those described in 2 and hence can be easily evaluated at compile time.
4. The value type of the alternatives (and of the ternary expression as a whole) is String.
5. No null appears anywhere in the ternary expression.
6. No boxing or unboxing is done anywhere in the ternary expression.
7. There is no explicit non-String cast anywhere in the ternary expression and there is no cast at all of the result of ternary expression (i.e. not even (String)).

then Eclipse tells me for each field as described in 2 that it "cannot be resolved to a variable" and for each method local variable that it "cannot be resolved or is not a field", although the Compiler from OpenJDK 11 successfully compiles the code.

(I suppose there are more aspects and details)

Here is a minimalistic example class:

public class C {
	final String s1 = "";

	public void m(Object s) {
		final boolean b = false;
		final String s2 = "";

		m(b? s1 : s2);
	}
}

b cannot be resolved or is not a field
s1 cannot be resolved to a variable
s2 cannot be resolved or is not a field


"About Eclipse IDE" says:

Eclipse IDE for Java Developers (includes Incubating components)

Version: 2020-12 RC1 (4.18.0 RC1)
Build id: 20201203-2138

(This is Linux with OpenJDK 11.)

7498217498122 URL = https://bugs.eclipse.org/bugs/show_bug.cgi?id=569626

Assuming the current 1st line in the StyledText is partially cropped, if one switches from fixed line height (default) to variable line height (eg by enabling word wrap), then the visible area moves for no good reason. It will basically move the content so that the top line is the one that was previously just after the "partial" one.
In cases where there is no layout change (eg enabling word wrap when there is nothing long enough to wrap), nothing should move, or it gives an impression of being "jumpy".
This does quite visibly affect code minings as well, which use the setLineVerticalIndent() method.

Cause seems to be the use of --limit-modules in the plug-in .classpath.

Seen with Eclipse 4.15 and also with:

Eclipse SDK
Version: 2020-12 (4.18)
Build id: I20201103-0030

Background:

We compile and run with Java 11, basing our product on Eclipse 4.15. This requires use of --limit-modules in some of our plug-ins due to JDT shipping JDI classes with itself, prior to Eclipse 4.17 (bug 565417).

We recently tried to move also our test plug-ins to compile with JLS 11, but ran into the problem here; we cannot run the tests from the IDE any more, due to countless unresolvable bundles. We "resolved" this by adding more JDK modules to the respective test plug-ins (modules that are not needed for the compilation of those plug-ins). However as soon as another (new or changed) bundle requires something else from the JDK, we'll see the same problem again.

7498217498122 URL = https://bugs.eclipse.org/bugs/show_bug.cgi?id=569345

Problem is that "F3" or ctrl-click on typescript/angular types will always result in a popup because of duplicate declarations found.
I find this a bit annoying because you have always an extra handling instead of directly going to it.

In OpenDeclarationHyperlinkDetector the code in the method detectHyperlinks is:

CompletableFuture.allOf(
LanguageServiceAccessor
.getLanguageServers(textViewer.getDocument(), capabilities -> Boolean.TRUE.equals(capabilities.getDefinitionProvider()))
.thenAcceptAsync(languageServers ->
languageServers.stream().map(ls -> ls.getTextDocumentService().definition(LSPEclipseUtils.toDefinitionParams(params))).forEach(allFutures::add)
),
LanguageServiceAccessor
.getLanguageServers(textViewer.getDocument(), OpenDeclarationHyperlinkDetector::isTypeDefinitionProvider)
.thenAcceptAsync(languageServers ->
languageServers.stream().map(ls -> ls.getTextDocumentService().typeDefinition(LSPEclipseUtils.toTypeDefinitionParams(params))).forEach(allFutures::add)
)
)

and then in the end returns for "Definition" and "typeDefinition" both the exact same links

this is because the angular/typescript language services says that it is a DefinitionProvider and it is also a TypeDefinitonProvider

(node_modules/typescript-language-server/lib/lsp-server.js i think where that is defined)

if i disable 1 of the above in that code, then it kind of works, i see different behavior

lets say i have 3 things

MyOwn TS files (class/superclass and so on)
Angluar classes (like SimpleChanges)
ESx classes (like completions of Object.keys() and opening "keys")

if i disable the "definition" part

my own TS file stuff (opening super class, or jumping to a function declaration) is working fine
Angular classes don't open (you don't jump to the definition files)
Object show still a list of 3 items (and those are really different because it matches on es5.d.ts, es2015.core.d.ts and 2017.d.ts)
Object.keys jumps directly to the 2017 but i guess that is something that is not in 2015 or es5..

if i disable the typeDefinition part
then my own are still fine and also angular classes open just fine
Object and Object.keys now shows a list of 2 items point to the same file (es5) but they are on 2 different locations

if i compare it with VisualStudioCode then it works like the second one (so disabling the typeDefintion part)

if i quickly patch the code of OpenDeclarationHyperlinkDetector so use a map to filter/distinct stuff based on the location:

Map<Either<Location, LocationLink>,LSBasedHyperlink> allLinks = Collections.synchronizedMap(new HashMap<>());

synchronized (allLinks) {
links.forEach(link -> allLinks.put(link.getLocation(), link));
}

return allLinks.values().toArray(new IHyperlink[allLinks.size()]);

then it always works, then it is kind of if i had disabled the typeDefinition part.

maybe it is nicer to let LSBasedHyperlink have an equals and hashcode impl that just redirects it to the location (which has equals/hashcode)
then you can use in the method toHyperlinks of OpenDeclarationHyperlinkDetector in the streaming i guess 1 call (distinct())

7498217498122 URL = https://bugs.eclipse.org/bugs/show_bug.cgi?id=569009

I submitted a PR against JKube [1] for a one character fix and the ECA validation failed even though "I know I've signed the ECA". It took almost an hour to figure out what the problems were and get it fixed. This was too difficult and too much overhead to contribute to Eclipse IMHO.

It turned out the problem was a combination of:

1. I have multiple email addresses on my GitHub account, I think it only accepts the one I use for Eclipse signup even though they're all clearly "me".
2. I had forgotten to actually sign the commit.
3. When I did sign the commit I accidentally committed it with a different email.
4. Other tools accepted the commit as signed but ECA didn't until I tried again.

This would have been much quicker if the ECA gave a simple summary of the individual checks it does and whether or not the commit passed them individually, e.g. green/red checkmarks for:

 - Whether the email was recognized.
 - Whether the commit is signed.
 - Whether the commit signing matches the committer.

This would have pointed me directly to the problem(s) each time instead of guessing what it didn't like.

[1] https://github.com/eclipse/jkube/pull/481

7498217498122 URL = https://bugs.eclipse.org/bugs/show_bug.cgi?id=568926

The platform debug process console has actions that can disable console activation on standard or error output. This is exceedingly useful when using a different console page (e.g. the stack trace console), since output from whatever is being debugged won't activate the process console page.

The CDT build console needs similar actions, since it will pop up (very unasked for), even over the process console page.

Action for standard out of the platform debug console: org.eclipse.debug.internal.ui.views.console.ShowStandardOutAction

Preference is: org.eclipse.debug.internal.ui.preferences.IDebugPreferenceConstants.CONSOLE_OPEN_ON_OUT

org.eclipse.debug.ui/ui/org/eclipse/debug/internal/ui/DebugUIPreferenceInitializer.java:                prefs.setDefault(IDebugPreferenceConstants.CONSOLE_OPEN_ON_OUT, true);
org.eclipse.debug.ui/ui/org/eclipse/debug/internal/ui/preferences/ConsolePreferencePage.java:           addField(new BooleanFieldEditor(IDebugPreferenceConstants.CONSOLE_OPEN_ON_OUT, DebugPreferencesMessages.ConsolePreferencePage_Show__Console_View_when_there_is_program_output_3, SWT.NONE, getFieldEditorParent()));
org.eclipse.debug.ui/ui/org/eclipse/debug/internal/ui/preferences/IDebugPreferenceConstants.java:       String CONSOLE_OPEN_ON_OUT= "DEBUG.consoleOpenOnOut"; //$NON-NLS-1$
org.eclipse.debug.ui/ui/org/eclipse/debug/internal/ui/views/console/ProcessConsole.java:                } else if (property.equals(IDebugPreferenceConstants.CONSOLE_OPEN_ON_OUT)) {
org.eclipse.debug.ui/ui/org/eclipse/debug/internal/ui/views/console/ProcessConsole.java:                        boolean activateOnOut = store.getBoolean(IDebugPreferenceConstants.CONSOLE_OPEN_ON_OUT);
org.eclipse.debug.ui/ui/org/eclipse/debug/internal/ui/views/console/ProcessConsole.java:                                        store.getBoolean(IDebugPreferenceConstants.CONSOLE_OPEN_ON_OUT));
org.eclipse.debug.ui/ui/org/eclipse/debug/internal/ui/views/console/ShowStandardOutAction.java:         return IDebugPreferenceConstants.CONSOLE_OPEN_ON_OUT;

Something similar should be added for the CDT build console, if nothing can be re-used from platform debug.

7498217498122 URL = https://bugs.eclipse.org/bugs/show_bug.cgi?id=569296

Bug 564379 has led to a new problem:

The current implementation of AbstractNotificationPopup always creates a dummy Shell in the constructor to be used as parent.

Hence, the condition to use the parent shell is always true.

The problem is, that this dummy shell has default coordinates, and the popup appears - totally unexpected - somewhere in the center of the screen.

This went by unnoticed because the 

    org.eclipse.ui.internal.dialogs.ViewsPreferencePage.NotificationPopUp

implementation forcefully overwrites the parent shell in the constructor:

    setParentShell(PlatformUI.getWorkbench().
        getActiveWorkbenchWindow().getShell());

7498217498122 URL = https://bugs.eclipse.org/bugs/show_bug.cgi?id=569188

If a model contains a choice point loop (any chain of transitions which leads from a choice point back to it, most basic case: A choice point self transition), a StackOverflowError is thrown.

The error also occures if the loop is closed via choice points outside of the current substate graph (through entry and exit points).

Instead of the StackOverflow I would expect a warning for choice point loops.

While in most cases choice point loops are probably unintended there might be cases in which they are valid as long as their conditions always lead to an exit state.

7498217498122 URL = https://bugs.eclipse.org/bugs/show_bug.cgi?id=568965

Synchronizing Maven Artifacts may fail on Windows with
> java.lang.IllegalStateException: cannot delete X:\some\workspace\file.jar

It turns out that jar files might be left open by the JDT Indexer even beyond the Indexer has finished, because closing the jar files is left to garbage collection.

As it turns out to be almost impossible to probably close all files as soon as the Indexer stops (see bug#406170 for example), beyond stopping the Indexer we also need to force garbage collection within TEA for the maven sync.

7498217498122 URL = https://bugs.eclipse.org/bugs/show_bug.cgi?id=569144

When creating a new build directory and simply issuing "make" twice, the entire source code is compiled twice. Expected behaviour would be to not recompile anything upon the second invocation of "make".

The cause is a simple ordering mistake in CMakeLists.txt. An option that governs string list generation (FORTE_LINKED_STRINGDICT) is declared only after subdirectory "src" has been processed. Thus on the first run, the src subdirectory uses an empty (i.e. false/OFF) value for FORTE_LINKED_STRINGDICT and configures the build system and compiler command lines accordingly.

Later, after the damage is done, the main CMakeLists.txt file declares that option and sets its default value to ON, which is saved in the CMake cache. But it doesn't take effect retroactively.

When issuing "make" a second time, the value for FORTE_LINKED_STRINGDICT is taken from the cache, thus now it is ON while subdirectory "src" is processed, changing all compiler commands, leading to the recompile.

7498217498122 URL = https://bugs.eclipse.org/bugs/show_bug.cgi?id=569025

Currenty the Floating Server is implemented with the help of Jetty. 
Passage codebase has dedicated plug-in, where a server get's raw http request and deals with it. 

Besides http request reading, it also configures dipatchable actions, which is not a Jetty-thing, this logic belongs to Passage. 

The request handling should implement no business logic.

7498217498122 URL = https://bugs.eclipse.org/bugs/show_bug.cgi?id=569687

Currently, the location of the source MANIFEST.MF file cannot be configured. The PackagePluginMojo class, in its updateManifest() method, always tries to get that file from the META-INF folder in the project base dir:

> File mfile = new File(project.getBasedir(), "META-INF/MANIFEST.MF");

After loading the manifest and modifying its Bundle-Version property, it is written to the target directory and then used for the creation of the jar file itself. 

Should the location of the source MANIFEST.MF file be configurable, you could use a MANIFEST.MF file in the PDE containing Maven properties, filter them using maven and then pass the result to the packaging plugin.

7498217498122 URL = https://bugs.eclipse.org/bugs/show_bug.cgi?id=569652

Not a new bug, but first noticed in 5.10:

Steps to reproduce:

0. Run on a case-insensitive filesystem.
1. Have a tag named "Tag1".
2. Choose "Create tag..." on some commit from the history view.
3. Type "TAg10" in the tag name field. (Yes, with capital 'A'.)

Expected result:

* The text field contains the text "Tag10"

Actual result:

* The text field contains the text "0Tag1"

The dialog checks while typing whether there is an existing tag matching the input. Once you've typed "TAg1", it finds the existing tag "Tag1". Because "Tag1" != "TAg1", it'll update the text field and set it to "Tag1". The caret jumps to the beginning, and when the '0' key is hit, we end up with "0Tag1".

7498217498122 URL = https://bugs.eclipse.org/bugs/show_bug.cgi?id=569124

Created attachment 284871 [details]
screenshot

As code mining is enabled when you open a java file it starts to find the usages and implementations etc. So when you open each file you have to wait up to 2 seconds to be able to edit the file because lines' locations are changing and you can't even click where you wish.
I think it's better to index the whole project when we open it and then persis the index of code mining so when we open a file there is no need to mine the code.
Especially it annoys when you close and reopen a file and you have to wait again.
This could make the project opening process longer but waiting every time I open a file is unacceptable.

7498217498122 URL = https://bugs.eclipse.org/bugs/show_bug.cgi?id=569723

In org.eclipse.emf.cdo.explorer.ui.checkouts.actions.OpenWithActionProvider.openEditor() there's this code:

        CDOCheckout checkout = CDOExplorerUtil.getCheckout(view);
        CDOTransaction transaction = checkout != null ? checkout.openTransaction() : view.getSession().openTransaction(view.getBranch());

If the checkout is created for a historical time (e.g., a tag or timeStamp!=0) the call to checkout.openTransaction() fails.

7498217498122 URL = https://bugs.eclipse.org/bugs/show_bug.cgi?id=569417

Currently, if a Remote Condition Miner is configured, but fails to connect to floating server, then the whole access chain fails. 

We should allow a miner to be unoperable, as it actually stays in a green zone: disfuction means less permissions. 

In the case a mining service is broken, a worning must be appended to diagnostic, and mining should proceed with the next service without failure.

7498217498122 URL = https://bugs.eclipse.org/bugs/show_bug.cgi?id=569669

Downloaded 2020-12 RC2 and tried a simple Chromium run. I get this error:

"SWT.CHROMIUM style was used but chromium.swt win32 (or CEF binaries) fragment/jar is missing."

The binaries are there, but I noticed that the versions in chromium.properties don't match the actual filenames. The properties file has:

00=chromium-3071/chromium_subp-4936r26.exe
01=chromium-3071/chromium_swt_4936r26.dll
02=chromium-3071/swt-chromium-win32-4936r26.dll

The actual files in the folder are:

chromium-3071/chromium_subp-4940r23.exe
chromium-3071/chromium_swt_4940r23.dll
chromium-3071/swt-chromium-win32-4940r23.dll

Changing the properties file resolves the issue.

7498217498122 URL = https://bugs.eclipse.org/bugs/show_bug.cgi?id=569110

Created attachment 284865 [details]
Short record of this issue, from the main eclipse application

Hi, 

Since the last MacOs update, I've been facing issues in my RCP application. 
Those issues are often related to SWT table / tree using StyledCellLabelProvider. 

Here is the current issue: 
I have a table using a StyledCellLabelProvider, a search bar above the table and a viewer filter to bind the search and the displayed content. 
Before Big Sur, the following peace of code was enough to refresh the table and apply the search: 

searchObservableValue.addValueChangeListener(e -> {
            Display.getDefault().asyncExec(() -> {
                String search = searchObservableValue.getValue().toLowerCase();
                fieldToFilter.clear();
                fieldsObservable.stream()
                        .filter(field -> !field.getName().toLowerCase().contains(search))
                        .forEach(fieldToFilter::add);
                viewer.refresh();
            });
        });

-> With the refresh(), the viewer filter is recomputed and apply the new values to filter. 

Now, with Big Sur, I also have to manually call a viewer.redraw(), else the viewer doesn't display the expected elements. 

Ive been able to reproduce the exacte same behavior in the default eclipse application (launch configuration wizard 2020-09, see attachment).


Since this issue only happens when the table / tree uses a StyledCellLabelProvider, I believe that this issue is probably related to this one: https://bugs.eclipse.org/bugs/show_bug.cgi?id=565969

7498217498122 URL = https://bugs.eclipse.org/bugs/show_bug.cgi?id=569280

7498217498122 URL = https://bugs.eclipse.org/bugs/show_bug.cgi?id=569352

From time to time we have our tests failing (https://ci.eclipse.org/passage/job/passage-base/735/console) on reading hardware state (disks part) on virtual machines, which are configured to not have ones. 

Even if a simplest hardware expression is to be assessed, like 'os.family=*', the whole hardware state is scanned, and the failure is inevitable. 

The truth is, is a hardware state property is not asked, it can legally be absent. 

Thus, we can isolate each part of hardware state reading to contribute only those values. which we managed to scan. 

It will allow to avoid failures for cases, when potentially failed property even not necessary.

7498217498122 URL = https://bugs.eclipse.org/bugs/show_bug.cgi?id=569253

Currently, in Sirius 6.4.0, the arrange at opening ignores other elements. It is expected to have possible overlap with other existing nodes (this is another improvement). But the top-left margins added for the new layouted elements should be the same than during the arrange all.

There is for example an overlap between the container title and new nodes in it.

Steps to reproduce:
* Create a modeling project with data from "gitSiriusRepo\org.eclipse.sirius\plugins\org.eclipse.sirius.tests.junit\data\unit\layout\withELK"
* Open the diagram "diagramWithContainer" of "packageForArrangeSelectionTest"
* Launch an arrange all
* Expected: No overlap between containers title and content of theses containers: OK
* Save
* Close the diagram
* Replace the My.ecore file with the file contained in "gitSiriusRepo\org.eclipse.sirius\plugins\org.eclipse.sirius.tests.junit\data\unit\layout\withELK\replace"
* Open the diagram "diagramWithContainer"
* Expected: No overlap between containers title and content of theses containers: KO
    * New class "Class2_2_3" overlaps, or almost, the title of container "p2_2". This class should be on the same location than "Class2_2_1".
    * New class "Class1_4" overlaps title of container "p1". This class should be on the same location than "Class1_2" and new class "Class1_3" should be on the same location than "Class1_1".

There are 2 "TODO" comments in org.eclipse.sirius.tests.unit.diagram.layout.SimpleELKLayoutTest.testArrangeAtOpening1(), and 2 others similar in testArrangeAtOpening2(), to validate this change.

In case if the Requirement's resliction level is below error, no Permission (successfully evaluated Condition) is created. As the Condition's source is actually a target for acquiring, we cannot acquire feature, on which `warning` or `info` restriction is declared.

7498217498122 URL = https://bugs.eclipse.org/bugs/show_bug.cgi?id=568905

On MacOS BigSur 11.0.1, if you add any listener to SWT.EraseItem, then Tables will no longer render checkboxes or images correctly.

This was not true in 10.15 Catalina. I have confirmed this behavior with SWT 4.16 and 4.17. An example which reproduces this is below:

import org.eclipse.swt.SWT;
import org.eclipse.swt.layout.FillLayout;
import org.eclipse.swt.widgets.Display;
import org.eclipse.swt.widgets.Group;
import org.eclipse.swt.widgets.Shell;
import org.eclipse.swt.widgets.Table;
import org.eclipse.swt.widgets.TableItem;

public class MacBigSurTable {
	public static void main(String[] args) {
		Display display = Display.getDefault();
		Shell underTest = new Shell(display, SWT.SHELL_TRIM);
		underTest.setLayout(new FillLayout());
		createTable(underTest, "works");
		Table brokenTable = createTable(underTest, "broken");
		brokenTable.addListener(SWT.EraseItem, e -> {
			// breaks the table even if it doesn't do anything at all
		});

		underTest.open();
		while (!underTest.isDisposed()) {
			if (!display.readAndDispatch()) {
				display.sleep();
			}
		}
	}

	private static Table createTable(Shell parent, String name) {
		Group group = new Group(parent, SWT.SHADOW_ETCHED_IN);
		group.setText(name);
		group.setLayout(new FillLayout());

		Table table = new Table(group, SWT.BORDER | SWT.V_SCROLL | SWT.MULTI | SWT.FULL_SELECTION | SWT.CHECK);
		TableItem item = new TableItem(table, SWT.NONE);
		item.setText("Test");
		return table;
	}
}

7498217498122 URL = https://bugs.eclipse.org/bugs/show_bug.cgi?id=568912

In the below code

public class Cls1 {

	public static void process(int i) {              
		var t = switch (i) {        
	        case 0:                  
	             return 1; // Error - Quick Fix works only if the return statement is surrounded in curly braces                       
	        default:
                     yield 100;
		}; 
        	System.out.println(t);
	}   
	public static void main(String[] args) {
		process(1);
		process(0);
		process(2);
	}                                   
}

The fix for bug 563209 works only if the case statements are in a block (surrounded by curly braces) and at least one return value (yield) is present.

The fix does not work for the above code. It shouild be provided for the above code.

Created attachment 284855 [details]
CDT console disabled in settings

Noticed while testing bug 486033 patch, using CDT master (but the behavior is not new).

AS IS:

1) Go to Preferences -> C/C++ -> Build -> Console.
2) Disable *both* "Open console when building" and "Bring console to top when building".
3) Open Console view and open "Java stack trace console".
4) Build a trivial C++ projects.
5) The C++ console is shown, "Java stack trace console" is hidden.

TO BE:

In step 5) CDT console shouldn't be shown over Java console.

Note: the current preference is implemented in the way that it only checks if the *entire* Console view should be shown on top of the stack (or not), but it *always* pushes CDT page on top in the Console view itself.

I will push a patch.

7498217498122 URL = https://bugs.eclipse.org/bugs/show_bug.cgi?id=569031

1. Create a new class and add enough lines for a scrollbar to appear.
2. Scroll with the mouse wheel. Note the speed (number of lines per scroll tick). For me it's exactly 3.
3. Restart Eclipse. The file will be open. Repeat step 2. For me it scrolls ~1.5-2 lines per tick.
4. Close the file and reopen it, the fast scrolling is restored.

The scroll speed should always be the faster one.

7498217498122 URL = https://bugs.eclipse.org/bugs/show_bug.cgi?id=569062

During Capella Project Creation there is an error that is raised if the name contains some special characters such as "<". 
These special characters are the same as those authorized by the host OS for a file/folder creation.

The rest of the characters are thus authorized by the OS, but might raise issues in a EMF-XML serialization context .
Some authorized characters such as "#", "%", "$" raise a runtime error during project creation.

These characters should not be allowed.

7498217498122 URL = https://bugs.eclipse.org/bugs/show_bug.cgi?id=569010

Created attachment 284831 [details]
image shows a menu bar icon without and with template set to true

In order to support both MacOS light and dark themes menu bars, Apple recommends using a template NSImage. 

According to Apple's guidelines: "A template image discards color information and uses a mask to produce the appearance you see onscreen. Template images automatically adapt to the user’s appearance settings, so they look good on both dark and light menu bars, and when your menu bar extra is selected."
https://developer.apple.com/design/human-interface-guidelines/macos/extensions/menu-bar-extras/

Recent MacOS menu bars use black/white images (though color icons are still supported). In order to support the Apple's guidelines, SWT's TrayItem should set the template property to true.

7498217498122 URL = https://bugs.eclipse.org/bugs/show_bug.cgi?id=569252

The Generate All action which generate the DocumentStructure then the final Document (odt or docx) opens dialogs:
  1. a first dialog when the DocumentStructure is generated
  2. a second dialog when the final document (docx or odt) is generated.
  3. several error dialogs can be open too, if the generation failed
 
The goal of this bug is to provide an API without these dialogs and another one with these dialogs.
Our usecase is to be able to use this API without dialogs in job generating several documents in one user action.

7498217498122 URL = https://bugs.eclipse.org/bugs/show_bug.cgi?id=568981

IN ELK, for the label of ports, you can precise the location with "Port Label Placement" [1]. Two values are usefull: "INSIDE" or "OUTSIDE".
The result is like in ELK_insideOutsideSampleWithoutEdge.png (sometimes "NEXT_TO_PORT_IF_POSSIBLE" must be added to the previous values). With these values, the label is centered on the port, inside or outside of the node. This result is visible in ELK "Layout Graph" view with "insideOutsideSampleWithoutEdge.elkt"; or directly in ELK Demonstrators [2].

If an edge crosses the label, the label is automatically shifted to the corner, like in ELK_insideOutsideSampleWithEdge.png. This result is visible in ELK "Layout Graph" view with "insideOutsideSampleWithEdge.elkt"; or directly in ELK Demonstrators [3].

Unfortunately, the "corner location" is not a valid location in Sirius. So Sirius automatically uses an authorized location for the port label, not the same, and the result is often an overlap and/or a feeling of space too big, like in Sirius_insideOutsideSampleWithEdge.png. In the current version of Sirius, to avoid this kind of situation, the "Port Label Placement" is ignored and a fixed location is used. Code from org.eclipse.sirius.diagram.elk.ElkDiagramLayoutConnector.createPort(LayoutMapping, AbstractBorderItemEditPart, IGraphicalEditPart, ElkNode, Map<LayoutOptionTarget, Set<LayoutOption>>):
        // Set the location of port label fixed (indeed the location returned by ELK is currently not compatible with
        // Sirius constraint). The label is, by default, located centered below the port.
        elknode.setProperty(CoreOptions.PORT_LABELS_PLACEMENT, PortLabelPlacement.fixed());


This problem is linked to bug 550382 in Sirius 6.3.0. It has been reverted by bug 561385 in Sirius 6.3.1 as it has side effects.

The goals of this issue are:
* Implement fully the initial bug 550382 (by considering all aspects, a non exhaustive list is available in description of bug 561385)
* Verify that ELK "Port Label Placement" property [1], is correcty considered by Sirius: projet in "TestWithInsideOutsidePortLabel.zip" is a sample as starting point.

[1] https://www.eclipse.org/elk/reference/options/org-eclipse-elk-portLabels-placement.html

The Appveyor build is not really useful in the current state because it takes too long and gets cancelled most of the time so we want to switch to only one build per day. So please disable rolling builds and builds on push and enable the schedule in the General tab.

Please use the following crontab expression

0 3 * * *

(3 o'clock UTC every day)

As mentioned here: https://help.appveyor.com/discussions/questions/1172-scheduled-nightly-builds it is only possible to do this from the web interface.

Thanks

Sample program

The following program doesn't present compilation error when compiling in ECJ but it must not be compilable.

Program

public class A<T> {
  public void m() {
	C.m(B.m());
  }
}

public class B {
	public static <T> T m() {
		return null;
	}
}

public class C<T> {
	public static void m(C<?> c) {}
	public static void m(A<?> a) {}
}


Current Results

      No compilation issues.

Expected Results

      A.java:3: error: reference to m is ambiguous

Configuration

	Software

		O.S.: Deeping Linux 15.9 64bits
		ECJ: Eclipse Compiler for Java(TM) v20150120-1634, 3.10.2 (Eclipse Luna 4.4.2)

7498217498122 URL = https://bugs.eclipse.org/bugs/show_bug.cgi?id=568882

As part of our migration of GitHub bot credentials from the deprecated username/password to the username/token format, we are cleaning up Jenkins credentials.

Instead of credentials with random IDs (e.g. b6987280-6402-458f-bdd6-7affc2e360d4), human-readable credentials like "github-bot" should be used.

Please replace the following IDs in your various job configs/Jenkinsfiles like this:

* b6987280-6402-458f-bdd6-7affc2e360d4 => github-bot

* b87c83da-2209-4958-9666-6a5b0e9a071b => github-bot-token

* 7fb9f8f0-14bf-469a-9132-91db4dd80c48 => docker-login

Once the IDs are replaced, we will remove them.

I have an offline target platform and have tried various things to make the tycho buuld work and produce the desired result. The problem is always the executable feature. To build my offline target platform that I give to tycho I use a feature manifest file. If I add the feature org.eclipse.equinox.executable there - in included features - the export function creates entries for the launchers in the artifacts.jar but does not create an entry for the feature itself and also does not output a org.eclipse.equinox.executable.jar. Then during the tyoho build this jar is missing which leads to an error. 

I tried also create a separate additional p2-site just for the executable by using the FeaturesAndBundlesPublisher. (I added the the feature folder and a packed version of it there). This works fine and if I add this site to the tycho build, the build succeeds - but with the "disadvantage" that there is no launcher in the product (no eclipse.exe). I understand that this comes from the fact that the FeaturesAndBundlesPublisher works different then the feature.xml export function: it does not are for binaries, so the binaries in which the launchers are, are missing. 

So my simple question is what can I do to make a tycho build work just with offline links.

7498217498122 URL = https://bugs.eclipse.org/bugs/show_bug.cgi?id=569153

With bug 564758 we support server-side commit modifications. The committing client simply rolls back its transaction and waits for the new commit notification from the server. That works well except for new objects, which are detached during the rollback (i.e., they lose their identity).

7498217498122 URL = https://bugs.eclipse.org/bugs/show_bug.cgi?id=569730

Selecting something in download.eclipse.org and pressing archive leads to an info/error because of an insecure redirect. 

The insecure redirect is from https://download.eclipse.org/path-with-no-trailing-slash -> http://download.eclipse.org/path-with-no-trailing-slash/ i.e from a no trailing slash to the non-https site. The http:// immediately redirects to https://, but because of the temporary http:// the whole session is not secure and in Chrome 87, when this happens during a form submission you get an error message. See https://blog.chromium.org/2020/08/protecting-google-chrome-users-from.html for info.

7498217498122 URL = https://bugs.eclipse.org/bugs/show_bug.cgi?id=569246

The goals are to improve the API used to create a DocumentStructureTemplate:
   -  improve the viewprototype (classe PapyrusDocumentTemplateViewPrototype ) to be able to get the created DocumentStructureTemplate as result of the method instanciateOn instead of a boolean.  
   - implements the method PapyrusDocumentTemplateViewPrototype#instantiateOn(EObject owner, String name, boolean openCreatedView) in order to be able to create closed view
   		- currently the created editor is always opened
   - add a method to the viewprototype to be able to define the graphical context during the creation
   - create a RecordingCommand for the creation of the DocumentStructureTemplate to remove the anonymous creation command of AbstractCreateDocumentTemplateEditorCommand#execute

7498217498122 URL = https://bugs.eclipse.org/bugs/show_bug.cgi?id=569160

FloatingText would be nice to be used in platform, e.g. in wizards. 

To use this widget in platform code it should be must be moved to platform. I contacted Wim and Laurent and they support this idea.

We should create a new plug-in to host such new widgets. 

I suggest: "org.eclipse.jface.widgets"

7498217498122 URL = https://bugs.eclipse.org/bugs/show_bug.cgi?id=568923

Created attachment 284802 [details]
Screenshot showing the main toolbar button.

See attached screenshot "open_terminal_button.png".

This button should be visible at most in CDT perspectives. Adding CDT TM Terminal plug-ins to an application should not influence non-CDT perspectives.

The contribution is in: terminal/plugins/org.eclipse.tm.terminal.view.ui/plugin.xml

      <menuContribution locationURI="toolbar:org.eclipse.ui.main.toolbar?after=additions">
         <toolbar
               id="org.eclipse.tm.terminal.view.ui.toolbar"
               label="%toolbar.terminal.label">
	         <command
	               commandId="org.eclipse.tm.terminal.view.ui.command.launchToolbar"
	               icon="icons/eview16/console_view.png"
	               id="org.eclipse.tm.terminal.view.ui.commands.launchToolbar"
	               label="%command.launch.label"
	               style="push"
	               tooltip="%command.launch.tooltip">
	         </command>
         </toolbar>
      </menuContribution>
